[H Zhang> Second Zhang

Soviet New Economic Policy Restored 17

Abolishing the System of Rationing by Headcount

Free Buying and Selling at State-Fixed Prices

Reorganization of Political Departments in Collective Farms

(Moscow) Since 1929, Soviet Russia has implemented a rationing system as part of the Five-Year Plan, requiring all people to purchase bread and other daily necessities with ration coupons. Today, the Central Committee of the Communist Party, during a meeting, passed a resolution proposing to petition the People's Committee to abolish this system. If successful, Russia will revert to the New Economic Policy of 1921, when the first attempt to implement pure communism failed, and private trade was partially restored. (Reuters, 28th)

(Moscow) The Central Committee of the Soviet Communist Party held its annual plenary session from the 25th to the 28th of this month, discussing two issues: the abolition of the rationing system for bread and other goods, and the reorganization of the political departments in state-owned farms and machine tractor stations. Several resolutions were passed. The introduction to the resolution on abolishing the system of rationing bread and other goods stated that this system was necessary at the beginning because small-scale agricultural production still dominated, with backward technology and weak productivity, while the demand for food in cities and industrial areas was increasing daily. Since the implementation of the First Five-Year Plan, cities have developed rapidly, national industrialization has progressed quickly, and the living conditions of the workers and peasants have improved daily, leading to a sharp increase in their demand for bread and other products, which agricultural production could not satisfy at the time. Now, large-scale mechanized agricultural production has been consolidated, and state-owned and collective farms have gained dominance, leading to a significant change in the situation. The state now has sufficient grain to supply the people with a free bread system, without the need for rationing. This old system must be abolished, as it is an important step in the development of Soviet trade. Once this system is abolished, the two different prices (i.e., the rationed price and the ordinary price) will disappear, and the state will use a single price, which will be roughly the average between the existing high ordinary selling price and the low rationed selling price. However, this method will inevitably raise the price of bread significantly, so the Central Committee believes that the wages and salaries of workers should also be increased accordingly. The current regulations for collective farms selling goods will be retained, but all efforts must be made to prohibit bread speculation. The resolutions passed by the plenary session are as follows:

(1) From January 1, 1935, abolish the system of rationing bread, flour, and grain, and allow state-owned and cooperative stores to engage in general free buying and selling of bread and other goods. (2) Abolish the current retail prices of bread, flour, and grain, and replace them with state-fixed unified retail prices. (3) From January 1, 1935, increase wages, salaries, scholarships, and subsidies, and instruct the People's Committee to determine the extent of this increase. (4) People who previously used the rationing system for bread when supplying agricultural raw materials to the state should have this system abolished. In the future, areas selling agricultural raw materials must also implement a bread-buying system, and the state must increase the prices at which it purchases these raw materials. (5) Conduct large-scale trading of feed. (6) Some state-owned and cooperative commodities must be expanded immediately to engage in the sale of bread. (7) Formulate a plan for how to supply flour and grain to trading agencies, so that bread trading can proceed smoothly everywhere, and the needs of the people can be fully met. The resolution further stated that the abolition of rationing, the implementation of bread trading and state-fixed consistent and stable prices, and the future possibility of continuing to reduce these prices and the prices of industrial products, will allow the prosperity of the workers and peasants to continue to rise. This method is now possible because the collective farming system has triumphed, and agriculture has generally developed. At the same time, this method, based on the continued strengthening of the Soviet ruble currency system and the increasing expansion of trade between cities and villages, can further promote the greater development of agriculture and industry.

The resolution of the National Congress on the political departments of collective farms and machine tractor stations indicated that the establishment of these political departments was intended to resolve the difficulties encountered by the Party in carrying out the socialist transformation of rural areas. At the same time, it was also necessary to consolidate the political position of state-owned farms and machine tractor stations, to strengthen their political role in rural areas, and to generally improve their political and economic work. In the past two years, 3,368 political departments have been established in machine tractor stations, and 2,8021 in state-owned farms. The Party has carefully selected 25,000 staff members to work hard and eliminate all their shortcomings. The results can be illustrated by examples, such as the fact that many active collective farmers who were not previously Party members have now gathered around the Party, striving to fight against class enemies, preserve the assets of collective farms and the state, and fulfill the obligations that farmers should fulfill to the state. In general, anti-Soviet elements and enemies of collective farming who had infiltrated collective and state-owned farms to engage in sabotage have now been exposed, and most have been expelled. Collective farms have become a solid and invincible force, and they have integrated three-quarters of the farms in the country, with their cultivated area accounting for 90% of the country's total. In the past two years, Soviet agriculture has had 137,000 tractors, 18,000 combine harvesters, 63,000 horse-drawn and tractor-drawn seeders, 24,000 threshing machines, 343,000 various harvesting machines, and 25,000 trucks. At present, there are a total of 240,000 collective farms, 3,500 machine tractor stations, and 5,000 state-owned farms. They have a total of 281,000 tractors, 33,000 combine harvesters, 34,000 trucks, 845,000 horse-drawn and tractor-drawn seeders, 129,000 threshing machines, and 2,085,000 various harvesting machines. In the past two years, the work of these machines has been far better than in the past. In 1933, tractors cultivated 35 million hectares of land, while this year it is 55 million hectares. Last year, combine harvesters harvested 533,000 hectares of crops, while this year it is 1,576,000 hectares. The completion of spring sowing this year was 15 to 24 days earlier than last year. The harvesting work this year is far better than in previous years. Although the weather this year is poor, the harvest in some southern regions is no weaker than last year. The completion of the grain payment plan in 1934 was six weeks earlier than last year. Collective farmers now firmly understand that their obligations to the state should be fulfilled first. The slogan of striving for the happiness of Bolshevik collective farms and collective farmers has been deeply rooted in the hearts of collective farmers, and they regard it as a part of their daily lives and as a plan for their actual work. All of this is the result of the Party's correct policies and the rapid improvement of concrete leadership in rural areas. Political departments are a special form of Party organization. They are backed by the entire strength and authority of the Party and the economic power of machine tractor stations. Therefore, they have made important achievements in promoting the transformation of backward sectors of socialist construction (i.e., agriculture) into advanced sectors. However, according to experience, there are many problems in rural political leadership, so the existence of political departments alone is not enough. Now, in order to lead the entire work of collective farms (political, economic, cultural, etc.), normal Party and Soviet organs (which handle all administrative, economic, cultural, and financial work) must be consolidated. The Central Committee plenum recognized that the establishment of political departments in the past was entirely appropriate, and they have played an important role in clearing up shortcomings. At the same time, it resolved as follows: (1) The political departments of machine tractor stations should be transformed into ordinary Party organizations and incorporated into the existing district Party committees to achieve the above-mentioned goals. (2) If the area of each district is particularly large, it should be divided into several new districts, and the political departments should be incorporated. At the same time, the leadership of each primary Party organization should be transferred to the district Party committees. (3) In addition to the first secretary, the district Party committees in larger agricultural areas should have a second secretary. (4) The district Party committees should have an agricultural department, and each machine tractor station should have a deputy director for political affairs. All existing staff members of the political departments should remain in the districts to work. (5) Instruct the Politburo to thoroughly implement this resolution by March 1, 1935. (6) The system of political departments in state-owned farms should remain unchanged. The resolution further stated that although the economic strength of collective farms has been consolidated, there are still shortcomings in their work. A portion of collective farms still have wealthy elements mixed in, and their phenomena of sabotage have not yet been broken. According to the experience of grain payment this year, due to the sabotage of class enemies, some areas suffered huge losses during harvesting, threshing, and storage. At the same time, there are phenomena of poor work organization and insufficient utilization of tractors, threshing machines, and combine harvesters. Rural Communist Party members still suffer from political myopia and lax work habits, so these class enemies can still operate as usual. The district Party committees should use this winter to further consolidate collective farms, unite active collective farmers who are not Party members, improve the work of collective farm boards and chairmen, strengthen the role and value of collective farmers' meetings, and unite them around the Party. (TASS, 29th)

Overseas Delegation Arrives in Jinan

(Jinan) Zheng Qimiao and 24 other overseas delegates to the Fifth National Congress have arrived in Jinan for a visit and are scheduled to depart for Beiping on the 30th. (Special dispatch, 29th)

Yugoslavia's Memorandum to the League of Nations 18

Proving Hungary's Collusion with Terrorist Groups

Responsible for the Marseille Assassination

(Geneva) On the 22nd of this month, Yugoslav Foreign Minister Jevtić submitted an application to the League of Nations Council regarding the issue of political responsibility for the Marseille assassination, requesting the Executive Yuan to handle the case. Tonight, the Yugoslav Permanent Representative to the League of Nations, Fotitch, submitted a memorandum to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Avenol, strongly proving that Hungarian officials colluded with terrorists (i.e., the Ustaše, an organization formed by Croatian exiles). It is claimed that when the terrorists began their activities, they were personally trained by Hungarian army officers. Some terrorists were housed in the Fries Barracks in Békés, Hungary, until 1931. Afterward, Hungary established several training centers, the most famous of which was organized by Béla Székászi in Jankapuszta (near the Hungarian border with Yugoslavia). The recruitment, selection, and training of terrorists were all conducted within Hungary, and the Hungarian authorities facilitated the terrorists' possession of a large amount of military equipment and explosives. The memorandum pointed out that when the perpetrators of the Marseille assassination left Hungary, their passports were issued by the Hungarian authorities, and that the Ustaše printed its own currency, and its members wore uniforms and practiced openly. This was also acknowledged by Hungary in its note verbale of April 26 this year. The origin of the group's substantial funds must be thoroughly investigated. The memorandum went on to detail how the Yugoslav government had requested Hungary through diplomatic channels to stop the activities of terrorists, but the Hungarian government had consistently evaded the issue. The memorandum concluded by stating, "The Hungarian government bears a heavy responsibility. The Yugoslav government believes that it is an international duty of the utmost importance to reveal this to the highest international organization" (i.e., the League of Nations). (Havas, 28th)

(Geneva) After Yugoslavia's documents to the League of Nations were published, the Hungarian delegation immediately announced Hungary's position on the matter to international journalists. They first stated that the Hungarian delegation had not yet had the opportunity to formally respond to Yugoslavia's accusations, but generally and firmly denied them. The Hungarian government's response did not address each point, but only pointed out that Yugoslavia's actions were aimed at defaming Hungary's reputation. The claim in the Yugoslav memorandum that the Hungarian government was involved in the Marseille assassination was entirely fabricated. Hungary had no prior knowledge of the matter, and the perpetrators did not forcibly reside in Hungary. The Bulgarian government initially stated that the perpetrators came to Hungary from Bulgaria, but then retracted this statement. It is true that three people lived in Hungary before the Marseille tragedy, but the other perpetrators all came from other countries. The instigator of the case was not within Hungary. The Hungarian government has repeatedly notified the Yugoslav government of the situation in Jankapuszta. Hungary has also notified the League of Nations that the Hungarian government has been working since last spring to expel the Croatian outlaws in the area. However, although the area is called a "den," it is actually just a village with only 30 to 40 Croatian emigrants hiding there, but it was cleared on October 1. The Yugoslav government's request is no longer an issue, so there should be no further unfavorable actions against Hungary. This is what Hungary finds regrettable. (Guomin, 29th)

First Round of Negotiations Fails 20

Japan to Propose New Plan

Content Accompanied by Numerical Explanations

(London) It is expected that Japan will propose a new plan, or a revised version of the original plan, which will be the second step in the London Naval Talks. Japanese representative Yamamoto stated yesterday during a meeting with British Foreign Secretary Simon that he now has a new plan. It is reported that it contains detailed technical explanations and is accompanied by figures to demonstrate how Japan's original plan for equality and total tonnage can be compatible with Britain's suggestions for qualitative restrictions, not building defensive engineering construction on Pacific territories, and mutually notifying shipbuilding procedures. This plan is expected to be formally presented at the next meeting between British and Japanese representatives at the end of this week. At the same time, British Foreign Secretary Simon will visit US Chief Representative Davis. (Reuters, 29th)

(Tokyo) Tomorrow's meeting of the British-Japanese Expert Committee is the key to opening the naval preparatory talks. Japanese representative Rear Admiral Yamamoto plans to submit a new proposal at or immediately after the meeting. The main content is as follows: (1) Warships are divided into two major types: battleships, aircraft carriers, and Class A cruisers (10,000 tons, armed with 8-inch guns) are offensive weapons; Class B cruisers (10,000 tons, armed with 6-inch guns), destroyers, and submarines are defensive weapons. All aircraft carriers, offensive weapons, must be completely abolished. Battleships and Class A cruisers must be thoroughly reduced. The number and tonnage of various offensive warships must be required to be equal. Each country determines its common limit for defensive weapons, and within that limit, it is free to build various warships. (2) The overall maximum limit of offensive and defensive weapons that each country should possess is a common maximum limit. This limit should be reduced as much as possible to lighten the burden on the people as scheduled, realize mutual non-aggression, and achieve the purpose of disarmament. (Jiji, 29th)

(London) The Japanese delegation notified the British-Japanese Expert Committee on the 27th that it would adjourn on the 30th. As a result of the meeting on the 28th and 29th to discuss the response policy, it was decided to begin discussing numerical issues in order to advance the preparatory talks. Therefore, future talks will focus on negotiating numerical issues. (Jiji, 29th)

United States Insists on Naval Ratio System 21

Vincent Issues Declaration

(Washington) House Naval Affairs Committee Chairman Vincent declared today that if Japan insists on tearing up the naval treaty, Congress will allocate funds to prepare to build five ships for every three ships Japan builds. He personally will be the mover of this case and will request the necessary funds from Congress to implement this policy. We can ignore how Britain feels, but the United States cannot recognize US-Japanese naval equality because the area of territory that the United States must protect is larger than that of Japan. This would be tantamount to placing Japan in a superior position, and even at the cost of sacrificing the treaty, the United States cannot recognize Japan's naval equality. It is hoped that the Washington and London Treaties can remain effective. Americans certainly do not want a naval competition because taxpayers bear a heavy burden, and a huge navy is harmful to world peace, and the World War has already proven that the cost of armament is far less than the cost of war. It is reported that Vincent is one of the proposers of the Vincent-Trammell most superior naval bill. The House Naval Affairs Committee will demand to maintain the 5:5:3 naval ratio, and Vincent hopes that Japan can voluntarily withdraw its demand for equality. Vincent stated that if Japan insists on equality by threatening to break the treaty, the United States has no other choice but to maintain the 5:5:3 ratio in fact, that is, the United States builds five ships for every three ships Japan builds. Vincent also said that when the Washington and London Treaties were signed, Japan thought the ratio system was fair and accepted it, but now it considers this treaty unfair, shameful, and dangerous, and it is unknown what to make of it. (Guomin, 28th)

Westminster Abbey Royal Wedding 24

London was full of dignitaries and the public scrambled to watch

Distinguished guests' attire was colorful and dazzling

The grand occasion was unprecedented since the coronation of the British monarch

(London) The gathering in London of monarchs and royalty from various countries to celebrate the marriage of British Prince Duke of Kent was an unprecedented spectacle since the coronation of King George. Among them were King Haakon VII of Norway and Queen Maud, King Christian X of Denmark and Queen Louise, Prince Paul, Regent of Yugoslavia, and countless others from all over the country eager to witness the event. People began to gather along the route the newlyweds would travel from midnight onwards, and the crowds grew larger and larger after dawn. Roofs and windows were filled with people, and specially built viewing platforms were even more crowded. At 10:36 this morning, the Queen, accompanied by the Queen Mother, left Buckingham Palace in a specially designed carriage with large windows, leading the royal family. The crowd waiting outside the palace cheered wildly. The carriage was pulled by two chestnut-colored high-stepping horses, escorted by a guard cavalry. The carriages carrying other members of the royal family were also drawn by teams of two chestnut horses each.

Three groups of people went to Westminster Abbey this morning. The first group was the King and Queen of England. The second group was the bridegroom, the Duke of Kent, also in a carriage drawn by two chestnut horses, departing from St. James's Palace, accompanied by his brother, the Duke of York, and the Crown Prince, as his groomsmen. The third group was the bride, Princess Marina, escorted by her father, Prince Nicholas. The bride had a joyful expression, wearing a silver dress adorned with roses, the national flower of England. She wore a diamond tiara, covered by a veil, and carried a bouquet of white lilies. Her attendants all wore scarlet uniforms with gold trim. Their hair and wigs were dyed, making them dazzling. Along the route, sailors, marines, and guards from Scotland, Ireland, and Wales stood respectfully, commanded by Lieutenant General Gallant.

Westminster Abbey was filled with dignitaries. Male guests wore formal attire according to their rank, while female guests competed to be the most beautiful. The splendor of their attire was difficult to describe. The robes of the bishops were also noticed. The eight bridesmaids were particularly dazzling.

At 11:00 a.m., the ceremony began. As the bride slowly entered the hall, the choir sang loudly. The Bishop of Westminster introduced the guests to the bride and groom, followed by the Archbishop of Canterbury. After the introductions, hymns were sung and prayers were offered. Then, the Archbishop delivered a sermon, followed by more hymns and prayers. Finally, the national anthem was sung and the wedding march was played. The ceremony was elaborate and solemn, with orderly movements.

After the ceremony at Westminster Abbey, the bride and groom rode in a carriage to Buckingham Palace. The crowds along the streets cheered, their voices reaching over a mile away. The King and Queen of England also returned to the palace. The newlyweds then attended a Greek Orthodox wedding ceremony in the private chapel of Buckingham Palace, officiated by Germanos, the Archbishop of the Greek Orthodox Church in London. It was also quiet and orderly. The newlyweds exchanged vows and rings. Those participating in the ceremony included members of the British royal family and royalty from foreign countries who came to offer their congratulations. After the ceremony, the newlyweds attended a wedding banquet at Buckingham Palace. Later, at 3:30 p.m., they rode in a carriage drawn by famous horses to Paddington Station. Along the way, crowds were still densely packed to watch. At 4:20 p.m., the newlyweds took a five-carriage royal train to Birmingham, arriving safely at 6:20 p.m. They then proceeded by car to Himley Hall, where they plan to spend part of their honeymoon.

Today, King George, the Crown Prince, and the groom all wore naval uniforms. The groom arrived at Westminster Abbey first, while the bride was late. The groom looked anxious. The Crown Prince also seemed uneasy about it. However, when the bride arrived, the groom's face lit up. The bride entered the hall, escorted by her father, in a silver wedding dress that sparkled brilliantly. The train of her dress was twelve feet long. She bowed her head and slowly walked to the altar. When the "obey" clause was used during the wedding ceremony, the bride's reply of "I will" was soft and gentle, only audible to those in the front row. The groom answered in a clear and firm voice. When the groom took off his wedding ring and placed it on the bride's finger, the hall was silent. At 11:14 a.m., the Archbishop declared the bride and groom husband and wife. Then, the wedding bells rang loudly.

The Queen watched the wedding ceremony with her hands clasped, deeply moved, and frequently wiped away tears with a handkerchief. The Crown Prince gazed at the printed wedding program. After the bride and groom completed the ceremony, they appeared extremely happy. As they stepped down from the altar, the groom turned back and whispered a few words to the bride. As the King and Queen of England exited the church, they repeatedly bowed to the cheering crowd. At 11:50 a.m., the wedding ceremony was completed. The newlyweds then left the hall amidst cheers and boarded their carriage. (Reuters dispatch, 29th)

(London) During the British prince's wedding, the police managed street traffic in a very thoughtful manner. The city was divided into three zones, one of which stretched from Buckingham Palace to Westminster Abbey. From 8:00 this morning until the wedding ceremony, vehicles were generally not allowed to enter or exit except for those with special passes. According to foreign dispatches received by Reuters today, the radio broadcast of the prince's wedding was heard clearly in South Africa, Australia, New Zealand, and Canada. Athenian newspapers were filled with poems praising Princess Marina and England. Many Greeks hung color photos of the newlyweds adorned with the flags of Greece and England and wished the newlyweds happiness and England prosperity. There were banquets throughout the country to celebrate. The Greek government sent a telegram of congratulations to Prince Nicholas today. (Reuters dispatch, 29th)

British Expats Celebrate Enthusiastically 25

(London) Today, bells were rung all over the world to celebrate the marriage of British Prince Duke of Kent and Princess Marina of Greece. This was not only the case within the British Empire, but also in the capitals of European countries, where millions of people participated in the celebrations. Embassies, clubs, hotels, and other establishments had special facilities so that British expats and foreigners could remotely listen to the wedding ceremony at Westminster Abbey in England. According to a Reuters dispatch from New York, all New York newspapers published photos of the British prince and the Greek princess on their front pages, along with lengthy news reports detailing the wedding ceremony, the attire of the newlyweds, and the decorations of the streets of London. Today happened to be Thanksgiving Day in the United States, so the jubilant British expats were able to enjoy a full day of celebration. Many people got up at dawn to listen to the wedding news broadcast from London by radio. (Reuters dispatch, 29th)

(3) Wang Dongyuan's division and Wang's brigade captured Siyanqiao on the 25th, and the remnants of the bandits retreated to Jiujingdu, Fulu Cliff, and Jiepai. More than 2,000 of the bandits in the rearguard were severely attacked by Wang's brigade, resulting in many killed and captured. (4) Bandits and horses straggling within Linwu were closely pursued and suppressed by our local forces, and more than 30 bandit guns were captured, more than 30 bandits were captured, and many bandits were killed. (Special dispatch, 29th)

He dispatched various units to drive to it, and immediately recovered Yongcheng. Unexpectedly, when they pursued to Longjiazhai in Yong, the bandits attacked again at night, and a part of them fled to the Wangcun North River Basin. The two sides moved simultaneously at dawn on the 23rd, and after a fierce battle lasting five or six hours, the bandit forces were unable to withstand it and fled in disarray towards Dayong. They were pursued to Huixiping, and after another two hours of fierce battle, the bandits fled westward to Shidi. However, a part of He's bandits are still at Songbaichang and are currently being encircled and suppressed. (Special dispatch, 29th)

Xiao Qian Inspects the Situation in Liancheng and Tingzhou 29

(Fuzhou) Xiao Qian telegraphed the provincial government to report on the inspection of the situation in Liancheng and Tingzhou:

(1) Along the way from Longyan and Lianjiang, nine out of ten houses are empty, and there are no people or animals. The situation is particularly bad in Pengkou and Wenfang. It is feared that epidemics will occur next spring. (2) Although there are too many potholes on the Longting Highway, the roadbed is still solid, but it is uneven and the road surface is narrow. It is currently being built by the military industry in separate sections, but the labor costs are expensive. (3) The Longting Lian fortresses have been completed, and the fortress line is calm along the way. Outside the line, there are still remnants of bandits to be cleared. No one is farming, and a spring famine is expected. (4) There are many corpses on the road from Pengkou to Tingzhou, and no one is collecting them, which is very pitiful. (5) The boundaries of the fields seen along the way have not yet been demarcated. (6) The people deeply hate the bandits, and there are fewer strong men, and many old and weak people remain. The people still have ancient customs, etc. Based on this, Chen Yi has telegraphed Lin Sixian to pay attention to hygiene and earnestly prevent epidemics, and to properly plan for agricultural relief, and to notify the mobile medical teams to treat the sick people at any time. At the same time, he telegraphed the Ministry of Health in Nanjing to request experts to go to the recovered areas to investigate and prevent epidemics. (Central News Agency dispatch, 29th)

Chiang Orders the Dissolution of the General Headquarters of Various Routes in Five Provinces by the End of the Month 72

The remaining bandit dens in Fujian and Jiangxi must be recovered within a limited time.

A chart of the command system for the pacification zones has been established.

Telegraphic instructions have been issued for handling local post-war affairs.

Hankou Correspondence: The military campaign against bandits in the five provinces of Jiangxi, Guangdong, Fujian, Hunan, and Hubei has come to an end since the Jiangxi bandits fled west. The National Government specifically ordered the abolition of the General Headquarters of the East, West, South, and North Routes, as well as the General Headquarters of the Reserve Army, on the 27th. Gu Zhutong and Chiang Ting-wen were appointed as the Pacification Directors of Jiangxi and Fujian, respectively. Chiang Kai-shek's telegraphic orders also arrived in Hunan, Hubei, and other provinces at the same time, specifying the dates for the dissolution of the various General Headquarters and the recovery of bandit nests, as well as the future course of action. The original telegram is as follows: "Now that the remnants of the Jiangnan bandits have fled west and there are few scattered bandits left in the original bandit areas, it is imperative to redeploy forces to pursue and suppress them separately, with the aim of eradicating them as soon as possible. In addition to appointing He Jian as the Commander-in-Chief of the bandit suppression forces, leading the troops in Hunan, as well as the Xue and Zhou units, and the bandit suppression troops of various provinces, to pursue and block them separately, with the aim of annihilating them, the various bandit nests in Jiangxi and Fujian that have not yet been recovered must be recovered by the end of November, and fortifications must be completed. All previous combat orders for the Southeast, Northwest, East, and West Route Armies, as well as the Reserve Army, of the bandit suppression forces in the five provinces of Jiangxi, Guangdong, Fujian, Hunan, and Hubei, shall be cancelled on November 30th. Starting from December 1st, separate pacification zones shall be established, with deadlines for eradicating the remaining bandits, completing highways, organizing local areas, training the people, and handling post-war affairs in the bandit areas. In addition to submitting a request to the National Government and establishing a chart of the pacification zones and command system, this order is hereby issued for your compliance. However, before the implementation of the pacification measures, all troops must continue to complete their original missions. [Seal of Chiang Kai-shek] (28th)"

Hankou Chamber of Commerce Cables Ministry of Finance to Strive for Cash Transportation to Hankou 73

Financial Disturbances Throughout the City; Relief Efforts Are Difficult to Alleviate

Also Requests the Headquarters to Advocate for the Shipping of Huai Salt by Steamship

Hankou Correspondence: Since the Ministry of Finance issued a new order restricting the transportation of cash to Xiamen, Shantou, Qingdao, Hankou, and other ports, a major disturbance has occurred in the Hankou market. The Shanghai notes have plummeted, requiring a surcharge of over 17 yuan per thousand yuan. Discount rates have also increased sharply. Financial institutions throughout the city are in a state of panic, and other businesses are also greatly affected. The Hankou General Chamber of Commerce, believing that this matter is of great importance to the prosperity of commerce, sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance on the 27th, requesting the swift transportation of cash for relief. The telegram reads: "To Minister Kong [Xiangxi] of the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing: The Ministry's new order stipulates that cash transported to Xiamen, Shantou, Qingdao, Hankou, and other ports must be accompanied by passports. The news has caused panic throughout the city. Shanghai exchange rates have plummeted in recent days, and discount rates have risen sharply. At a time when local products are entering the market, the need for cash is particularly urgent. With the source restricted and circulation impeded, any delay in timing could lead to unforeseen changes. Shanghai and Shanghai are closely interconnected, and the impact will be indescribable. We earnestly request the Ministry to carefully consider the pros and cons and promptly order the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications to transport a large amount of cash to Hankou. If other commercial banks and money shops are required to obtain passports, the procedures should be simplified to provide relief and avert the crisis. Respectfully submitted, anxiously awaiting." Furthermore, the issue of Huai salt transportation is also a focal point of the dispute between the Hankou business community and the Ministry of Finance. Since Huai salt began to be transported by steamship, there has been the benefit of lower prices and faster speeds. Recently, in order to take into account the unemployed boatmen of Twelve Forts, the Ministry of Finance has ordered the Hubei salt merchants to switch to sail transport, which is not only more expensive but also takes longer and has a significant impact on people's livelihoods. The Chamber of Commerce has already cabled the Ministry to vigorously advocate for steamship transport. On the 28th, they also submitted a petition to the General Headquarters of the Three Provinces for bandit suppression, stating: "Human evolution has reached a point today where everything is moving towards lightness, efficiency, and convenience. As far as water transport is concerned, after the advent of steamships, sailing ships have lost their importance in transportation. To reverse this trend is to go against the tide and will not be tolerated by the times. Now, the salt authorities, in order to meet the demands of the fort residents, have ordered the transport merchants to switch to sail transport. By analogy, all steamship transport would be taken away from sailing ships. If we only consider the partial livelihood of the sailing ship owners, we must prohibit steamship transport altogether, which is absolutely impossible given the circumstances. Moreover, salt is a necessity for the people's livelihood, and steamship transport is more convenient and can reduce costs, thereby benefiting the people, which is a fact that cannot be concealed. We respectfully request Your Excellency to investigate and promptly telegram the Ministry of Finance to implement this request in order to emphasize the people's livelihood and maintain salt transport." (28th)

Large-Scale Air Defense Drill at Hangzhou Station 74

Six Bombers Set Off from Wusong to Fly to Hangzhou

Drill Completed at 5 AM as "Enemy Aircraft" Depart

Hangzhou Dispatch: In order to train employees in air defense knowledge and prevent unforeseen circumstances, the Joint Administration of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways specifically ordered personnel from the Jia Gate Section's Transportation, Engineering, Police Affairs, and other departments to conduct a large-scale air defense drill. After active preparation, the drill was carried out at Hangzhou City Station yesterday morning (29th) at 3:40 AM. The various circumstances are recorded below:

Preparations: A. Air defense organization: Divided into fire fighting teams, anti-poison teams, guard teams, train operation teams, communication teams, lighting control teams, engineering teams, and camouflage teams, respectively organized by Liao Mianqing, Stationmaster Li, and others, with Instructor Wu Shuchang, Deputy Instructors Cheng Xipei, Zhou Si, Wang Dekan, and Assistant Cheng Benhou. B. Drill locations: 1. Emergency assembly area: Hangzhou Station front square; 2. Shelter: Hangzhou Railway Hospital; 3. Temporary bandage station: Hangzhou Station fourth waiting room; 4. Burning site: opposite the Hangzhou Station platform. C. Enemy situation assumed: According to a telephone report from the Wusong surveillance post, six enemy bombers were heading towards Hangzhou from Wusong at 3:40 AM on the 29th, flying at an altitude of approximately 2,500 meters and a speed of 280 kilometers per hour. They arrived in Hangzhou at 4:00 AM and dropped several incendiary bombs at the station.

Drill Execution: At 3:45 AM on the 29th, Hangzhou City Station received an emergency report from Jiaxing Station that six enemy aircraft were passing through Jiaxing and heading towards Hangzhou. At 3:55 AM, Hangzhou Station received another urgent telegram from Changan Station in Haining that the enemy aircraft had passed through Changan. Upon receiving the first report, Hangzhou Station immediately sounded the alarm and assembled personnel from various teams. Upon receiving the second report, it urgently sounded the emergency bell, turned off all lights in the station, and the various teams were dispatched simultaneously. At 4:00 AM, the enemy aircraft arrived, circling in the sky and dropping bombs. At the same time, disguised rioters took the opportunity to bomb the tracks and station buildings with explosives. When the guard team's sentries discovered the rioters, they rushed to suppress them and immediately arrested them. At the same time, it was discovered that the tracks had been damaged, and a rescue train was dispatched to repair them. At that time, a bamboo shed next to the station was set on fire by a bomb (simulated). The fire brigade immediately went to extinguish it. Meanwhile, the rescue team rescued and bandaged the injured and sent them to the hospital. At 4:45 AM, the enemy aircraft had left, the alarm was cancelled, the tracks were repaired, the fire was extinguished, and the lights were restored to their original state. The drill was then completed. (29th)

However, the total consumption of opium by licensed smokers is used as the amount of opium paste sold by each opium paste shop, which is said to be less than one-third. According to people in the opium paste industry, official sales are not smooth, which is due to the activity of private opium. They will find ways to petition the county association to strictly prohibit it in order to maintain the prohibition policy.

Wuxi 77

Provincial Committee Secretly Investigates Private Opium Dens in Wuxi

No. 26, Yushan Chuanbang, North Gate, the Jiang's brothel, is a famous family of Ronghu pleasure boats, and the prostitution industry is at its peak. First, there was the famous courtesan A Feng, whose beauty rivaled the moon and whose reputation was unique. She was chosen by the people of the time as one of the Four Vajras, and she was also good at drinking, with the reputation of being a big drinker. When A Feng got married, she was replaced by "Feng Bao", whose eyes were bright and beautiful, and whose beauty was natural. Since the prohibition of prostitution, the brothel has relied on the patronage of regular customers, coupled with the popularity of pleasure boat cooking, so its livelihood is still not bad. Currently, there are three young prostitutes: Feng Zhu, Pan Di, and Xiu Bao (i.e., Xue Xue). Recently, the Provincial Anti-Opium Committee sent personnel to Wuxi to secretly investigate private opium smoking and selling, which was very strict. It was found that the Jiang's brothel was providing opium for people to smoke, and it was reported to the County Anti-Opium Committee, which notified the Public Security Bureau. At about 12:00 on the previous night, the police were dispatched to search the Jiang's residence and seized three opium pipes, two opium lamps, a large jar of opium paste, several decks of cards, and a copy of Jiang's opium prohibition license, and arrested the madam Jiang Qiu (Da A Sao), the prostitutes Jiang Huiying (Pan Di), Jiang Lianying (Feng Zhu), Wang Yunxing (Xiu Bao), the maid Wang Meixiu, the female servant Li Qian, and the boatman Yang Dongsheng, and took them to the bureau for interrogation and detention by the County Anti-Opium Committee. At the same time, the bureau also arrested Du Pan Gen at No. 9, Gengdu Bridge, South Gate, Zhao Ren Gen at No. 66, North Chang Street, Tang Huifen at Huilong Bridge, Shao A Qiao at No. 11, Huntang Lane, North Gate, Gu Zhou and Gu San Da at No. 12, Cao Zhang and Zhao Zhang at No. 19, Xiaosifang Lane, Zhang Hu, Zhu A Yuan, Li A Da, Chen Tingjing, and Jiang Qingping in the Malu District, Guo Hui, Cao Hua, Wu Zhao, Du Mingyuan, Li A Bao, Su A Gen, and Shen Zhongchu in Zhongzheng Road, and Wu Rongda, Xue Yonghe, Ji A Bing, Zhang Wang, and Liu Wang at No. 16, Jiulong Lane, and took them to the bureau for interrogation and detention.

(5) Send a letter to the Municipal Education Bureau to instruct all schools in the city to recommend representatives to participate. (6) The chairman of the assembly shall be recommended by the Executive Committee. (7) Request the Director of the Security Office, Yang Xiaotian, to attend and report on the circumstances of the Zhaohe Uprising in the name of the association. (8) Issue a public announcement on the Zhaohe warship uprising anniversary.

French Concession Levies Inspection Fees 88

The Mechanical Industries Association Requests Negotiations

Document Submitted to the Government

Since the French Concession's Municipal Council promulgated the Regulations for the Management of Steam Engines and Machinery, it has openly levied inspection fees on the Hongxing Hosiery Factory to inspect our country's factories. The Mechanical Industries Association of national commodity factories in this city has therefore submitted a document to the Ministry of Industry of the National Government and the Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday, requesting strict negotiations regarding inspection rights to prevent disguised encroachment. The original text reads: "Submitted for the authorities of the French Concession deliberately encroaching upon our country's factory inspection rights and levying steam boiler inspection fees, requesting strict negotiations to protect sovereignty. On April 16th of this year, the member Hongxing Hosiery Factory reported that on the 6th of this month, the French Concession Health Bureau sent personnel, accompanied by the Fire Brigade, carrying machinery to inspect the factory's boiler, injecting 120 pounds of cold water, and left satisfied. Unexpectedly, today (April 10th)

a notice in French was sent, stating that an inspection fee and other expenses totaling seventy yuan should be paid annually, which is deeply surprising. As it concerns national sovereignty, the factory is unwilling to rashly set a precedent," and attached a photo of the French notice to the association. The association immediately submitted a report to your ministry, requesting reasonable negotiations, and the French Concession authorities also stopped collecting the fees. Unexpectedly, after half a year, the old matter was brought up again, and a notice was issued to the Hongxing Hosiery Factory, first collecting half the fee. The factory recently reported that the special zone's factory inspection issue is under negotiation. In April of this year, the French Concession Municipal Council suddenly inspected the factory's boiler and levied an annual inspection fee of seventy yuan. As it concerns our country's sovereignty, it was reported to your association and forwarded to the Nanjing Ministry of Industry, the Shanghai Municipal Government, and the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession, requesting protests. Unexpectedly, on the 22nd of this month, another notice in French was received from the French Concession Municipal Council, still intending to levy an inspection fee of thirty-five yuan for half a year, claiming it is based on the recently promulgated Regulations for the Management of Steam Boilers in the French Concession. The factory believes that money is a small matter, but sovereignty is a major issue. Whether the inspection fee should be paid has not been dared to be decided without authorization. Therefore, a special letter is sent to your association to forward it to the Nanjing Ministry of Industry and the Shanghai Municipal Government, requesting a clear instruction to follow. Because the factory is under the accumulated prestige of foreigners and easily makes mistakes, it should request the government to provide protection. A photo of the French notice is attached to the association. It is found that the Regulations for the Management of Steam Engines and Machinery, promulgated by the French Concession authorities this spring, are sufficient to seize our country's sovereignty. After being revised and promulgated recently, the Hongxing Hosiery Factory was asked to pay half a year's inspection fee first, and their deliberate encroachment on sovereignty is obvious. Our government is now working hard to recover lost sovereignty, and such disguised acts of encroachment cannot be tolerated. A photo of the French notice and a copy of the Regulations for the Management of Steam Engines and Machinery published in the Shanghai Commercial News are attached, and a document is submitted to your ministry for review and verification. A strict negotiation is requested to protect sovereignty, and instructions are requested so that factories in the concession can be protected and complied with, which would be a great convenience.

Representatives from Twelve Provinces' Private Postal Bureaus 90

Continued Emergency Meeting Yesterday

Resolved to Petition the National Government to Extend the Closure by Five Years

Since the Ministry of Transportation ordered the Directorate General of Posts to instruct private postal bureaus to cease operations, private postal businesses in various ports across the country have been in a state of panic. They all believe that once closed down, more than 100,000 people engaged in private postal services across the country would be innocently unemployed. Therefore, they have successively sent representatives to Shanghai to discuss the aftermath. An emergency meeting was held once a few days ago. Considering the seriousness of the matter, more than 100 representatives from twelve provinces, including Jiangsu and Zhejiang, gathered at the private postal bureau in this city at 4:00 PM yesterday for a second emergency meeting, resolving to petition the Central National Government to extend the closure by five years and deciding to hold a large-scale petition to the Shanghai Municipal Government and Municipal Party Headquarters on Wednesday and Thursday next week. The details are as follows, as learned by the East China News Agency reporter:

Emergency Meeting: The national private postal industry held its second emergency meeting at the private postal bureau on Li Xian Gua Street at 4:00 PM yesterday. Attendees included representatives from Shanghai, Yin Yuantong and Hua Yunqing; representatives from Nanjing, Yue Xiechen; representatives from Yangzhou, Chen Jieren; representatives from Zhenjiang, Zhang Shiyu; representatives from Ningbo, Liu Shousheng, Xu Shan, Chen Bangxian, and Zhang Liansheng; representatives from Sichuan, Zeng Senchang and Yu Geshun; representatives from Jiaxing, Shen Baifu, Ying Chunyu, Shen Guoliang, Li Bingquan, Chen Kangning, Xu Ashun, and Zhu Qingfu; representatives from Yantai, Wang Ziying and Qiu Zhensheng; representatives from Datuantuan, Fang Xianzhang; representatives from Zhoupu, Chen Shaozhong; representatives from Hangzhou, Wu Bingshang, Wang Dabin, Yu Kedong, Zhuang Gengtang, Wang Zuhao, and Zhang Guitang; representatives from Fuzhou, Li Baosheng; representatives from Wenzhou, Wang Yongzeng; representatives from Suzhou, Ren Shiting; representatives from Shantou, Wang Hengfu, Fang Baokang, Fang Baoxiang, Zhang Xiling, Dong Pinsen, and Huang Huinan; representatives from Xiamen, Ge Tianxiang; and representatives from Hankou and other ports, totaling more than 100 people.

Petition for Extension: The meeting was chaired by Yin Yuantong, a representative from Shanghai. After the meeting was formally opened, the representatives jointly discussed the matter. As a result, it was decided to draft a petition immediately and, before December 10th, send three representatives to Beijing to submit the petition to various agencies of the National Government, the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Transportation, requesting them to consider the difficulties of the people and extend the deadline by five years before closing down. If necessary, representatives from the national private postal industry will be convened again to make a large-scale petition to the Fifth Plenary Session, not stopping until the goal is achieved.

Scheduled Petition: In addition to resolving to petition the National Government to extend the closure by five years, the meeting also decided to gather representatives from all parties next Wednesday and Thursday to launch a large-scale petition to the Shanghai Municipal Government, Municipal Party Headquarters, and Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and issue a letter to compatriots, explaining the difficulties of closing down private postal bureaus and the convenience of having private postal bureaus, hoping that compatriots across the country will sympathize and demand relief. The discussion dispersed at around 7:00 PM.

Assistance from All Parties: According to Chairman Yin Yuantong, speaking to the East China News Agency reporter, the history of this industry has long been revealed in various newspapers. The news of the Ministry of Transportation's order to close down our industry came suddenly and in a hurry. It is known that there are more than 1,000 private postal bureaus across the country, with more than 100,000 employees. If they are closed down, it will not only be inconvenient for compatriots, but how will such a large number of unemployed people be taken care of? Wouldn't that be sitting and waiting for death? Therefore, we most hope that the authorities will consider the difficulties of the people and have appropriate party methods to enable 100,000 people to be able to work and maintain their lives. Therefore, this industry is drafting a petition to request the central government to extend the deadline by five years, so that during this period, they can gradually change industries or find their own ways to close down. Furthermore, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association, and various industry associations all believe that this matter is a serious issue and will also hold meetings to discuss and decide on assistance plans.

Results of Adultery Law Review 91

Women's Groups Fiercely Oppose

Believing It Is More Ridiculous Than Before

Will Still Strive for Consensus

Women's friendship groups held a joint emergency meeting and fiercely opposed the decision of the Legislative Yuan's Criminal Law and Legal System Committee on the 28th to review Article 239 of the Criminal Law, which revised the original text to "Anyone who commits adultery with a married person shall be sentenced to imprisonment of not more than one year," believing that the wording was vague and even more ridiculous than before. They also issued a declaration calling on women across the country to make a final effort to fight for it. The original text is recorded as follows: "To the women compatriots across the country, for thousands of years, the various inhuman oppressions suffered by women in our country have been entirely based on legal inequality. In order to eliminate obstacles to family happiness and maintain social morality, there has been this struggle for Article 239 of the Criminal Law. Unexpectedly, the results of the Legislative Yuan's review are even more ridiculous than before, and the wording is also vague. 'Only those who commit adultery with a spouse are punished, but those who commit adultery are not punished.' This is not only unfair, but also seems to intentionally encourage spouses to commit adultery with others. Our association and others advocate restoring the original draft or adding the five words 'those who commit adultery are also the same' to the review and amendment. As it concerns family happiness and social morality, we respectfully hope that our women compatriots will urge the legislators to awaken and create impartial and selfless laws and regulations to promote the Chinese nation on the road to rejuvenation. Otherwise, with what we consider to be dangerous, our association and others will still strive for consensus, not stopping until the goal is achieved." The Chinese Women's League, the Chinese Women's Temperance Association, the Shanghai Women's Advancement Association, and the Chinese Women's Society.

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement Considers Transportation Issues 93

Plans to Send Experts to Study Management Methods

Now Submitted to Two Committees for Further Review

The Municipal Council's Transportation Committee has recently conducted detailed discussions on the traffic management plan within the settlement, and has listened to various reports and opinions. It was recently decided to request the Board of Directors to appoint a qualified traffic management specialist within the Police Department. This proposal was submitted to the Board of Directors for discussion on the 28th of this month and was decided to be submitted to the Police Committee and the Merit Committee for further review.

Points for Discussion: At the recent Transportation Committee meeting, Mr. G. Robinson was specially invited to participate in the discussion. Mr. Robinson pointed out the important points, namely: (1) To negotiate and cooperate with neighboring authorities; (2) To complete statistics and produce traffic maps; (3) Enforce existing regulations and add new regulations, with strict penalties; (4) Study new tools for traffic management; (5) Close cooperation between various departments in the bureau, with mutual consideration in all aspects of road excavation; (6) Appoint a traffic expert to formulate the implementation steps.

Appointing Experts: A committee member also advocated that a traffic engineer with experience and ability should be appointed. This person is urgently needed to manage traffic and should not be delayed due to financial problems.

Accident Statistics: According to the report submitted to the committee by the Chief of Police, the number of deaths caused by traffic accidents in this settlement in 1933 was 10.7 per 100,000, compared with 15.9 in New York, 16.5 in London, and 25.7 in Los Angeles. The number of injuries was also not high in comparison in this settlement. In 1929, the number of car licenses was 6,575, and the total number of traffic deaths that year was 141. By 1933, the number of cars was 9,367, and the number of deaths decreased to 107. The total number of accidents in 1924 was 6,085, and in 1933 it was 13,571. However, regarding statistical comparisons, it is still necessary to consider the speed of vehicles and the size of the area.

Cooperation Among Three Settlements: Regarding Mr. Robinson's first point, the chairman of the committee said that the three municipal government agencies are now discussing cooperation methods for public transportation. Regarding statistical methods, Mr. Robinson said that personnel could be sent to count on the road, or special electrical counting machines could be used, or movies could be taken at a certain speed. The Chief of Police said that since 1919, the number of vehicles has been recorded once a year at 16 locations within the settlement, each time for two days. As for the production of traffic maps, the Director of Public Works said that it is not difficult to create a map to show the number of vehicles passing through each item, but the difficulty lies in how to express the relationship between each vehicle.

Traffic Court: The discussion then turned to the impact of traffic congestion at one point on other points. It was generally agreed that it would be beneficial to compile statistics on points that are prone to congestion. As for the level of punishment for violations, it has been carefully considered that it is impossible to set up a special traffic court in this settlement to be in charge of this matter.

Traffic Signals: Regarding how to systematize the release and stop of vehicles at various points, it is impossible to implement without installing expensive automatic signaling devices, and it is rare to prevent horizontal traffic from running at the same time on one road in the United States today. The alternative is to allow vehicles to continue moving unimpeded on a fairly long stretch of road, but in Shanghai, the types of vehicles are different, and there are rickshaws, making implementation difficult. Perhaps the opening and closing of traffic lights at each point can be given precise timing regulations, but no matter what method is implemented, it must be carefully planned. The Chief of Police then said

, it is not easy to speed up traffic, mostly due to the form of the road and its narrowness. One-way Traffic: Mr. Robinson continued to describe the progress of traffic management tools over the past ten years, and said that the implementation of a detailed circular or one-way traffic system would definitely be beneficial in Shanghai. The Director of Public Works said that promoting the one-way traffic method is extremely beneficial, but it is feared that it will be opposed by the majority of residents and cannot be implemented. It seems that too much attention has been paid to the convenience of automobiles, and the convenience of public buses, trams, and rickshaws should also be considered, as the number of passengers in these types is far greater than those in

Page 10

automobiles. The lunch time is too uniform, resulting in congestion at noon, and attention should also be paid to the long-term parking of private cars on the road. It is his opinion that the current building regulations should be revised to ensure that houses have more open space for parking. It was also suggested that a one-way traffic system be implemented on certain roads, but only for cars, not for rickshaws, or that the one-way system be extended during busy hours. It is said that in a certain place in the United States, one-way traffic was tried and stopped after three months, and merchants requested to restore it. This system can be considered a good thing. Then a committee member said that the experience of merchants on Hankou Road does not consider this a good thing. Public Transportation: The discussion then turned to traffic management and its related aspects, recognizing that the main transportation system must be flexible in order to benefit the general public. The Director of Public Works said that the laying of tram tracks was adapted to the previous situation, and it is difficult to repave them. Today, trams are still a cheap means of transportation for most people. Although trolleybuses are more active, the cars cannot overtake the cars in front of them. Public buses are more flexible and better than trams, but the operating expenses are huge. The use of diesel engines can save expenses, but the import tax is also very high.

Studying the Situation: Regarding the employment of a traffic expert, Mr. Robinson continued to state that if this person is obtained to engage in specialized research, the existing equipment can be used to increase the convenience of vehicle travel. The expert must first study the local situation before proceeding with the improvement plan. A committee member advocated that this specialist should be permanently employed and work closely with the police.

Proposed Methods: After the above discussion, the committee thanked Mr. Robinson for his great assistance and then decided to recommend to the Board of Directors that a qualified traffic specialist be appointed within the Police Department. However, the chairman of the committee simultaneously stated that this recommendation does not contain any criticism of the personnel and effectiveness of the current traffic division of the Police Department.

The state-run China Merchants Bureau specially dispatched the Fair Steamer to Bangkok, Siam, on the 18th of this month, and the Anxing Steamer to Saigon, Annam, on the 24th of this month, both to load foreign rice ordered by Chinese merchants, not to open up foreign routes.

Fellow Villagers from Hunan in Shanghai Petition the Central Government 95

Send Senior Officials to Hunan to Supervise the Suppression of Remaining Bandits

And Appoint Representatives to Go to Beijing to Petition

More than 200 fellow villagers from Hunan in Shanghai, including Yang Shixun, He Bingkun, Zheng Yan, Zhang Qipei, and Shen Ruli, recently petitioned the Central Government and the National Government in a joint name regarding the issue of the Red Bandits' intrusion into Hunan and disturbing the villages, requesting that senior officials be dispatched to lead troops into Hunan to pursue and suppress the remaining bandits, and appointed representatives to bring the document to Beijing to petition. The original submission is recorded as follows: "Submitted to petition for the dispatch of officials to supervise the suppression, provide funds for disaster relief, and reduce and exempt taxes to save Hunan and relieve the suffering. Our province of Hunan has recently been disturbed by the intrusion of communist bandits from Jiangxi, and all counties that have been passed through have been burned and killed, with no one spared in terms of life and property. Although the central government has recently dispatched a large army to enter the territory to suppress them, it is difficult to achieve victory due to the lack of a leader. Therefore, it is requested to quickly dispatch senior officials to supervise the entire bandit suppression force to eradicate the root causes of the communist bandits and avoid proliferation. This is also the first thing. This year's drought in Hunan Province has spread to more than 60 counties, and the grass roots and tree bark in various places have long been used up for hunger relief. However, the taxes in Hunan Province have increased endlessly, causing the residents of the disaster-stricken areas to commit suicide if they are weak, and to join the bandits if they are strong. Without providing relief, how can the lives of the people be preserved? Therefore, it is requested to provide disaster relief and strictly order the authorities of Hunan Province to reduce and exempt taxes in the disaster areas to comply with the central government's political strategy of suppressing bandits and alleviating the suffering of the people. This is also the second thing. The Hunan militia has always been able to defend itself. Since the reorganization by the Hunan Province authorities two years ago, the remaining abandoned guns and remnants of soldiers have caused the Red Bandits to invade and have no way to defend themselves. Therefore, it is requested to strictly order the Hunan Provincial Party Bureau to return the original excellent guns of the militia and cancel the additional six million yuan in militia land tax in order to reorganize the militia and reduce the people's distress. This is also the third thing. The petitioners are from various counties in Hunan Province. Recently, frequent reports have been received from home, saying that entire families have fled, or that they have all been burned and killed, or that they have been donated and levied. Every word is the sound of blood and tears from their hometown. How can the entire family and the entire village endure long-term decay? Unable to do otherwise, they plead and petition the Central Government to quickly find ways to provide relief and relieve the suffering."

Opinions of the International Problems Research Society 97

Regarding the U.S. Proposal to Convene a Pacific Conference

The International Problems Research Society, a private group in this city, issued an English opinion on the recent non-official U.S. proposal to convene a Pacific Conference. The translation is as follows: "In view of the impending failure of the current London Naval Conference, the world has no choice but to seek other ways to resolve

this important and complex international problem, so as to avoid the crisis of naval competition. Anyone who understands the naval treaty issue knows that the establishment of the former naval treaties was based on certain political conditions, such as maintaining peace in the Far East and guaranteeing China's sovereignty, independence, and territorial and administrative integrity. Japan now demands naval equality with Britain and the United States, but refuses to discuss political issues in the Far East. It is no wonder that the London talks are about to fail. Recently, the non-official U.S. side has proposed convening a Pacific Conference, and Britain has also expressed its agreement, while Japan dismisses it with a smile. Does Japan intend to obtain naval equality by unilaterally announcing the cancellation of the naval treaty? Can naval issues be completely separated from political issues? If Japan is prepared to compete with Britain and the United States in naval armaments, then its strong attitude today must change. Otherwise, the common interests, peace, and security of the Pacific countries will be greatly affected. In this meeting, our country is naturally the most relevant country, because the rights of our country, which were jointly guaranteed by the Pacific countries twelve years ago, have been tragically trampled on since the September 18th Incident. We hope to correct the previous injustice, recover the lost land, and obtain a more complete guarantee in the future. Britain and the United States have now made it clear that the integrity of China's territory is the key to their Far East policy. On the Japanese side, although they want to achieve naval equality, they turn a deaf ear to the proposal of the Pacific Conference. If Japanese politicians take a long-term policy on guaranteeing peace in the Far East, they should warmly welcome the convening of this conference, because the desire of various countries for them has long been suspected. This meeting is giving them a chance to eliminate doubts and make a clear discussion on various issues of maintaining peace. Today, Japan takes an isolated policy, refuses to participate in political talks, and takes a haughty attitude towards the proposer, which can never lead to the resolution of important international issues. On the one hand, Japan will never be able to obtain considerable naval equality because of this, and on the other hand, it will bear the responsibility for the failure of the London Naval Conference."

Kong Xiangrong Discusses Measures to Complete Plugging of Yellow River Breach 98

Must be completed within the Lunar New Year period

So as not to delay the people's spring plowing next year

Central News Agency reports: News reports state that the water outside Changyuan County's city walls is one zhang higher than inside the city, posing a risk of the entire city being submerged. In response, Kong Xiangrong of the Yellow River Disaster Relief Committee's Labor Relief Team issued a written statement saying, "I just returned yesterday from supervising work at the Guantai Longmenkou and Jiugulu breach sites. Since the efforts to block the Guantai breach began, the water level has been visibly receding, and the source is gradually being blocked, so it shouldn't be that severe. I have already telegraphed Sang Ze-tong and Wang You-long, two members of our team stationed in the field, to personally investigate the situation in that county. All projects, including blocking the Guantai breach to cut off the flow, restoring embankments and plugging breaches at Jiugulu and other county locations, and plugging and dredging the interconnected waterways around Daniezhuang, are being undertaken simultaneously and progressing smoothly. Our team is aware that time is pressing, and the weather will soon turn cold and the ground freeze, making it difficult to obtain soil. Therefore, we are rigorously supervising the progress to ensure that the plugging is completed before the end of the Lunar New Year, with the goal of not delaying the people's spring plowing next year." It is also learned that Mr. Kong will return to the front lines soon to continue supervising the work.

Recent Trends in China's Shipping Industry 99

The purpose of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's new "Sihai" ships

A vital force amid the loss of shipping rights

The new "Sihai" ships built by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company are expected to arrive in Shanghai within the year, which will replenish tonnage for coastal shipping and provide a vital force for the industry. Yesterday, the reporter had the honor of speaking with Mr. Li Yunliang, Chief Auditor of the company, about the trends in the domestic shipping industry, the strength of foreign shipping along the coast and the Yangtze River, and proposals for cooperation in the shipping industry, which are of utmost importance. The details are recorded below.

Foreign Shipping Strength

Our country's offshore and inland rivers have convenient shipping conditions, but unfortunately, foreigners have become the dominant players. British merchant ships number over a hundred, with approximately 260,000 tons, concentrated in companies such as Jardine Matheson and Butterfield & Swire. Japanese merchant ships number thirty-five, with approximately 75,000 tons, owned by companies such as Nissin Kisen, Dalian Kisen, and Osaka Shosen Kaisha. The number of unscheduled liners operated by these three companies is even greater. The U.S. has the Yangtze Rapid Steamship Company, and France has the Compagnie Franco-Chinoise de Navigation, with a total of twelve ships and approximately 7,000 tons. The total tonnage is estimated to be over 350,000 tons. Steamships on the Yangtze River are 140,000 tons, accounting for seven-tenths of our Yangtze River transport. Offshore shipping routes are almost entirely owned by foreigners. In recent years, the reclaiming of shipping rights has been widely proclaimed. The Sino-Japanese Treaty of Commerce and Navigation, the Anglo-Chinese Mackay Treaty, and the Sino-American Treaty of Commerce and Navigation have all expired. The government should vigorously strive to fully regain the shipping rights that have been infringed upon. However, weak countries have no diplomacy. Whether or not shipping autonomy can be achieved is still uncertain.

National Shipping Decline

An investigation reveals that there are only 512 Chinese-owned ships with a tonnage of over 100 tons, totaling 380,000 gross tons, which is a very small percentage of the world's 70 million tons. Among them, only over 40 ships have a registered gross tonnage of over 2,000 tons, and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company accounts for one-third of these. The average age of the ships is approximately 34 years. In the last 15 years, only four new ships with a tonnage of over 2,000 tons have been built, and only ten with a tonnage of over 1,000 tons. The rest are small vessels. Furthermore, the number of ships lost each year is quite high, and the new construction may not even be enough to compensate for the losses. As for the slight increase in total tonnage in recent years, it is entirely due to the purchase of old ships from foreign merchants, which are old, poorly equipped, and slow, making it impossible to compete with foreign merchants.

China Merchants Resurgence

In the Yangtze River shipping industry, Chinese ships, British ships, and Japanese ships stand as three legs of a tripod. However, in ocean shipping, Chinese ships lag far behind. The Beiyang (Northern Seas) routes have ships such as the "Xin Shengjing" and "Xin Shuntian", and the Nanhua (Southern China) route has ships such as "Taiyuan" and "Jinan". Consequently, Chinese people traveling on the major north-south ocean routes still have to rely on foreign ships, resulting in the outflow of profits and creating a helpless situation. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company also took this into consideration when building the "Sihai" ships. Purchasing old ships at a cost of 1.3 million yuan per ship would have allowed the company to buy at least four or five ships. However, to revive coastal shipping and replenish near-sea trunk lines, which is an urgent need for national transportation, the company could not only focus on short-term profits. Therefore, it resolutely ordered these four ships from England. All operational plans have also been thoroughly reformed, and the company relies on the support of the Chinese people and the protection of the government for cargo and passenger business. By the end of this year, all four ships will be able to sail on the Nanyang (Southeast Asia) route. With this vital force, China's shipping industry can finally hold its head high to some extent.

Cooperative Endeavors

In March of this year, the Ministry of Communications convened a meeting of shipping merchants from across the country to discuss measures to promote the shipping industry. Although there were over 200 proposals, the most important one was the proposal for shipping cooperation. Under the leadership of the Ministry of Communications, the Shanghai Shipping Association and the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company jointly formed the China Shipping Cooperation Design Committee. Within six months, the committee had drafted a plan. Subsequently, the shipping industry will automatically establish a China Shipping Cooperative, and each shipping route will first form separate alliances, with the government providing supervision and protection. The current Shanghai-Taiwan, Shanghai-Yangzhou, and Shanghai-Tianjin routes will make the disorganized shipping industry, compelled by environmental needs, achieve a spirit of unity. If the situation can be guided to benefit them and promoted, removing obstacles, it is possible, because apart from a few companies such as China Merchants, Sanbei, and Zhengji, most of China's shipowners are extremely dispersed, with many companies owning only one or two ships. The competition is very fierce, and the exclusion is even worse. Freight rates are plummeting, and the cost of transporting coarse goods is sometimes as low as seven or eight cents per dan (unit of weight). If this continues, Chinese ships will be in a tragic situation, facing annihilation. Therefore, implementing cooperation is the only way to save the shipping industry. The government should provide supervision to prevent the evils of monopoly. In this way, the serious problems in the shipping industry can gradually be solved.
