Guichi County, 85% Disaster-Stricken, 85% Grain Taxed 103

The Appeal of the Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association

The Telegram of the Drought Relief Association

Guichi County, Anhui Province, has suffered severely from drought this year. According to an investigation by the Central Relief Committee, 83% of the area has been affected by the disaster. The members of the Anhui Provincial Government, after on-site inspection, determined that the actual percentage was 85%. However, Commissioner Qiu Cheng considered that the harvest was 58%, and therefore decided that 85% of the grain tax should be collected as usual. The Finance Committee of the county, the Fellow Villagers Associations in Qingdao, Beiping, Tianjin, and Shanghai have successively requested the Anhui authorities to correct this, but to no avail. Yesterday, the Shanghai Association again petitioned the Shanghai Drought Relief Association for assistance. The telegram from the Relief Association is as follows:

To Chairman Liu of the Anqing Provincial Government, Commissioner Mao of the Department of Finance, and Commissioner Xiang of Chizhou: According to a letter from the Guichi Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai, "Our county has suffered an extraordinarily severe drought. The Central Relief Committee's investigation found that 83% of the area has been affected. Commissioner Zhang Hongyou of the provincial government and the county magistrate conducted an on-site inspection and reported that the percentage affected was over 85%. However, Commissioner Sun Peijing, in assessing the autumn harvest, considered that there was a 58% harvest, and therefore decided that 85% of the grain tax should be collected as usual. The reasons for this error are: (1) The polder fields were not considered to be affected by the disaster. These fields only account for one-tenth of our county's arable land and are distributed among various 'bao' (administrative units). Even if they are considered unaffected, they are already calculated within the un-polderized fields affected in each 'bao'. There is no separate polder field area. This phrase should not be added to the assessment of the affected acreage in each 'bao' to deceive our people. (2) Miscellaneous grains were planted after the autumn harvest. Our county only received 30 shi (unit of volume) of buckwheat seeds from the Construction Department, which were distributed and planted, covering less than 200 mu (unit of area) of arable land. Moreover, due to drought and frost damage, how much can be harvested? Even if there is a thin harvest of millet and sorghum, it is purely for tenant farmers to survive and not pay the full rent, and it has nothing to do with landowners who pay grain tax. How can this be used to increase the harvest assessment? Furthermore, this point has already been reported to the Finance Department through the Commissioner, stating the error and requesting a correction. However, the assessment is still based on Commissioner Sun's decision, and the harvest is assessed at 58%, which has been submitted to the province for approval to begin collection. The disaster victims, who are on the verge of death, cannot bear this unjust tax." The Association has investigated and found that the drought this year is extraordinarily severe. The Association previously resolved to telegraph the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance of the National Government, informing them of the affected provinces and properly exempting the affected farmland from regular and surtaxes, which has been approved. Now, the county, with an 85% disaster situation, must pay 85% of the land tax, which does not seem like a way to show compassion for the disaster victims. It is requested that the Director-General, Chairman, and Commissioner investigate the two errors made by the Committee and correct them to show fairness. The disaster victims will be fortunate, and the region will be fortunate. Kong Xiangxi, Chairman of the Shanghai Drought Relief Association, Xu Shiying and Wang Zhengting, Vice-Chairmen, respectfully present this report.

And opening of the Second Representative Assembly

On the 28th, the Shanghai Postal Workers Union held the 12th Inauguration Ceremony of the Executive and Supervisory Committee members and the Second Representative Assembly at the Management Bureau. Over 200 people attended, including all Executive and Supervisory Committee members, representatives from various branches, and members. Dai Youheng, representative of the Municipal Party Department, and Zhu Xuefan, representative of the National Postal Workers General Union, were present as observers. Chairman Zhang Kechang presided over the meeting, with Xiao Qingshan recording. The meeting began with the ringing of the bell. We are honored to have representatives from the Municipal Party Department and the General Union present to provide guidance. We are especially excited to see the representative of the General Union here today. Since the members of the General Union resigned previously due to difficult circumstances, postal workers across the country suddenly lost their guidance, and the public was extremely apprehensive. Fortunately, the postal workers across the country, with their united strength, urged the authorities to become aware, and the outstanding issues were resolved. Furthermore, after the sincere appeals of friendly associations in various locations, the members of the General Union have announced their reinstatement. We feel especially gratified to see each other today. Furthermore, today, the members of this committee are being sworn in under the supervision of the Municipal Party Department and the General Union. We hope that all members, after taking office, will continue to work diligently on association affairs with the spirit of past administrations. We especially hope that all members will provide supervision at all times to ensure that association affairs will continue to develop." Then, all the Executive and Supervisory Committee members took the oath of office. Next, Dai Youheng, representative of the Municipal Party Department, delivered a speech, stating in brief: "Shanghai is the center of industry and commerce, so there are more labor unions than in other places. Among those that are sound both in form and in spirit, there are few besides the Postal Workers Union. I hope that you will continue to work hard to promote and develop it. I especially hope that the Executive and Supervisory Committee members will work diligently and loyally in their respective positions after taking office." Zhu Xuefan, representative of the National Postal Workers General Union, delivered a speech, stating in brief: "Since the establishment of the Postal Workers Union, the union has been organized in most parts of the country. We are very fortunate that the organization of postal workers, whether in terms of quantity or quality, is very sound. However, this has caused some people to pay attention, and they are concerned about the expansion of the postal workers' power, or even become jealous. Therefore, the resistance we have encountered is very great. To cope with this environment, we must continue to work hard. Today, the Executive and Supervisory Committee members are being sworn in. I hope that all members will be loyal to their duties and strive for the development of association affairs. I especially hope that Shanghai postal workers will not underestimate the greatest determination and hope that they should have, and work hard towards our goals. We are in this era not only to seek our own welfare, but also to unite postal workers across the country to seek the revival of the nation." The following matters were then discussed: (1) The General Union members have announced their reinstatement after being unanimously requested to stay by the whole country. How should this association express its opinion? It was resolved: sincerely support it. (2) Association members have traditionally relied on membership cards. Now, according to the order of the General Union, it is necessary to issue badges separately. How should this be handled? It was resolved: Pass the motion and issue badges separately. (3) The association has suggested to the authorities that a postal workers' hospital should be established, but it has not yet been realized. How should we promote its realization? Four Assassinations in Two Years, Resulting in Five Deaths 106

The Communist Assassination Squad Organized After the Beat-Dog Squad

Kuang Huian and Ten Other Criminals Interrogated Yesterday and Awaiting Sentencing

| The Court Was Heavily Guarded During Yesterday's Trial |

The tragedy that occurred at Renji Hospital on September 26th at 3:00 PM, in which three lives were taken, was carried out by Communist bandits. After the incident, the police authorities of the International Settlement mobilized their detectives to investigate. Within 24 hours, they cracked down on the assassination organization formed by the party, arrested Kuang Huian, the second-in-command of the gang, and ten other male and female accomplices, and seized a large number of firearms. Later, it was also confirmed that these individuals had assassinated numerous people in the International Settlement in the past two years. They were charged with endangering the Republic of China, premeditated murder, and violating the regulations on the prohibition of military firearms, and were prosecuted separately. The Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court has repeatedly held trials to investigate the facts of the various cases committed by Kuang and others. The facts of the cases have been repeatedly reported in the newspapers. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the Criminal Court President Yu Hua and two judges, Zhao Zhengzheng and Zhou Han, specially convened a collegial panel to conduct a public trial. Chief Prosecutor Wang Zhennan also attended the court to perform his duties. The investigation lasted until 5:00 PM, when the debate was declared closed, and the sentencing was scheduled for the afternoon of December 6th. The guards inside and outside the court were removed after the criminals were escorted back to the men's and women's detention centers in prison vans. Now, we will describe in detail the various cases committed by the assassination squad in the past two years, as well as the circumstances of the arrest, the cracking of the case, and the court trial.

Organizing the Assassination Squad: The Communist Party has always regarded riots and massacres as its main tasks. In the past, it secretly organized the "Beat-Dog Squad" in Shanghai, targeting police officers who were unfavorable to them. In recent years, law enforcement officials in this city have been assassinated numerous times. Two years ago, thanks to the efforts of the police officers from both the Chinese and international settlements, the "Beat-Dog Squad" was finally cracked down. Most of the members of the squad were arrested, sentenced according to law. However, there are still several people who should be executed by decapitation and are temporarily detained in the Western Prison, waiting for the order to be executed. After the "Beat-Dog Squad" was eliminated, the Communist leader Yao ordered the establishment of this assassination squad to continue the cruel acts of the "Beat-Dog Squad." Yao then ordered Kuang Huian, a native of Shantou, to direct his followers to carry out the work. Yao himself was in a position to issue orders, so the members of the squad could only approach Kuang and did not know who Yao was. All the weapons and firearms needed for the assassinations were issued by Kuang when needed. Kuang and his concubine, Lin Er-mei, a Cantonese, rented the upstairs of the Xinwenxiang Silver Shop at No. 112 Julai Road in the French Concession. The firearms were also stored there.

Four Assassination Cases: According to the investigation by the police, the first task of the group after it was created was the assassination of Ma Shaowu (also known as Lu Keqin), a secret agent of the former Municipal Public Security Bureau, on the night of June 14th of last year, in the small garden of Zhejiang Road. The participants were Kuang Huian, Meng Huating from Hubei, and four bandits who have been arrested and punished in Beijing and Shanghai. On June 9th of this year, Kuang was ordered by his leader Yao to harm Chen Jing, who succeeded Ma Shaowu. Therefore, on that day, he and his accomplices Zhao Xuan and Meng Huating from Hubei, Zhu Jinming from Anhui, and Zhang Mazi, who had already been arrested and imprisoned, ambushed him near Hankou Road and Guangxi Road. When Chen passed by, they opened fire. Chen fell to the ground after being hit by a bullet. Wang Jinrong, a Chinese constable numbered 558, who was on duty there, heard the sound and gave chase. Kuang and the others dared to resist arrest and shot and killed Constable Wang. Chen Jing recovered from his injuries and returned to Beijing after leaving Shanghai. This case was the second act of violence by these individuals. On the night of September 16th, Kuang, Zhao, Meng, and Zhu, together with Zhang Mazi, carried out their third assassination. They broke into the Qianji Inn on Shanxi Road and shot and wounded Xiong Guohua, who had served in the Northeast Volunteer Army and whom these individuals referred to as a traitor who colluded with the Japanese and puppet police in Guanwai (Northeast) to harm the volunteer army. Because the result was only that Xiong was injured, they were still not satisfied. After a ten-day interval, Kuang led Zhao, Meng, and others to break into a ward of Renji Hospital and kill him in his hospital bed. At the same time, two other people were killed: Wan Yuke, the detective guarding Xiong, and He Yongfu, the Chinese constable of the French Concession who was escorting a sick prisoner to the hospital for treatment. In total, they carried out four assassinations in two years, resulting in five deaths and one injury. They were extremely cruel.

The Course of Solving the Case: Since the Renji Hospital tragedy occurred, the military and police in this city have paid close attention. On the afternoon of September 27th, within one day, the firearms hiding place inside the Xinwenxiang Silver Shop was cracked down. Twenty-five various types of handguns, two Mauser pistols, 1,003 bullets, one steel vest, and one bayonet were seized. Kuang's concubine, Lin Er-mei, was also arrested there. Subsequently, Kuang, Zhao, Meng, and Zhu, and Tang Wanxuan, a native of Yangzhou, were arrested. An elderly woman from Ningbo, Li Yang, and her daughter-in-law, Li Zhou, from Hubei, were arrested because her husband (Li Yang's son) was also a member of the gang. This time, Yao ordered Kuang to order Zhao, Meng, and Zhu

to move into Room 13 of the Hongxiang Hotel on Avenue Edward VII, where they were arrested. In addition, Liu Jinrong, a worker at a certain yarn factory who is currently the director of the labor union, and Zhang Li, a female worker from Chongming in the same factory, were also detained because they had arranged to go to Hongxiang for a private meeting, involving them in suspicion. After a thorough investigation by the police, they were charged with endangering the Republic of China, violating the Emergency Law, violating the regulations on the prohibition of military firearms, and the crime of premeditated murder under Article 284 of the Criminal Law, and were prosecuted separately to the Second Branch of the High Court.

The Circumstances of the Trial: Yesterday afternoon, the collegial panel organized by Judge Yu brought Kuang and the other ten male and female defendants to court for a public trial. The facts of the crimes committed by the defendants had been repeatedly interrogated and clarified. Yesterday, they were interrogated one by one again, and then the debate began. First, Gan Jingxian, the lawyer representing the police, spoke, stating that Kuang, Zhao, Meng, and Zhu were all in important positions in the Communist Party, which constituted the crime of endangering the Republic of China and the repeated crime of premeditated murder. He requested that they be punished according to the law. Li Yang and Li Yang's daughter-in-law were highly suspected of being involved in the Communist Party, and Li Zhou had been arrested previously in connection with a Communist Party case. This time, Zhu Jinming confessed that she was again working in an important position in the Communist Party. As for Lin Er-mei, she not only hid military weapons under the bed and next to the pillow in her bedroom, but also was Kuang's wife, so she was obviously helping the Communist Party in its work. He requested that they all be given serious consideration. Although the remaining Tang Wanxuan, Liu Jinrong, and Zhang Li lacked direct evidence, he also requested that they be judged freely.

Sentencing Scheduled for the 6th: After the lawyers hired by the defendants and the lawyers appointed by the court to provide free defense debated one after another, Chief Prosecutor Wang Zhennan stood up and argued that, "As a result of the investigation of this case, it was not possible to actively prove the criminal behavior of Liu Jinrong and Zhang Li in going to the Hongxiang Hotel. The fact that Li Yang and Li Zhou are the family members of important Communist Party members is already clear. It is also impossible to fully prove whether Tang Buxuan is related to the Communist Party. Since Lin Er-mei is Kuang's wife and a large number of military weapons were hidden in her room, it is undeniable that she helped the Communist Party in its work. As for the four defendants, Kuang, Zhao, Meng, and Zhu, they have confessed to the charges of endangering the Republic of China and the various cases of murder and attempted murder, and they have been proven. The purpose of these people is similar to that of the 'Beat-Dog Squad' that was previously cracked down. They can be regarded as the second 'Beat-Dog Squad'. Therefore, they should be handled according to the established case of the 'Beat-Dog Squad'. He requested that the presiding judge make a judgment according to the law. After he finished speaking, Judge Yu announced that the sentencing would be held at 2:00 PM on December 6th. The defendants were then escorted back to the police station and women's prison for detention under heavy guard.

Jiahe Steamer's Three Abductees Sent Letters Home 107

Bandits Investigate Families' Circumstances

To Determine Ransom Standard

Since the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiahe steamer was hijacked, three crew members have been held for over twenty days. The company telegraphed authorities in Fujian, Guangdong, and the Navy Department for rescue, but their whereabouts remain unknown. The families of the crew members are extremely anxious. Yesterday, letters from the three abductees, sent from the bandits' lair to Shanghai, arrived. The bandits also dispatched their accomplices to investigate the financial circumstances of the three hostages, using this information to determine ransom amounts. Details are as follows:

Three Send Letters to Shanghai The Jiahe steamer's business director, Shen Qinxiang, accountant Li Xiaobin, and tallyman Ge Liangchen were abducted by pirates from Shanwei and held in the bandits' lair for over twenty days. Their families anxiously awaited news, preparing for rescue. Yesterday, the Shen, Li, and Ge families each received a letter mailed from Hong Kong. Upon inspection, the letters were indeed written by Shen and the others from within the bandits' lair and taken to Hong Kong for mailing by the bandits, so there was no clear or detailed return address.

Comfortable Living in the Bandit's Nest Upon opening the letters, the families confirmed the handwriting as their own. The letters stated that since arriving at the mountains (but not specifying the name of the mountain, etc.), their food and lodging were relatively comfortable, and they were not suffering. They asked their families to be patient and not rush, and after the situation was clarified, it could be resolved, and they could return home for a reunion. The families suspect the three are being held near Dapeng Bay, but they cannot communicate with them.

Content of the Letters

The content of the three letters differed. The letter from tallyman Ge Liangchen was addressed to his widowed mother, and its tone was particularly poignant. He stated that their Shanghai residence was only a rented attic, and he was already two months behind on rent when he was abducted. He asked his mother to plead with the landlord to wait until he was released and returned to Shanghai to pay the rent. The letter from accountant Li Xiaobin advised his family not to worry, stating that the bandits were treating them well and there was no injustice. He said the bandits needed to conduct a thorough investigation of each hostage's family circumstances, and he hoped his family's poverty would be considered. The most important part of the letter from business director Shen Qinxiang instructed his family that if the bandits sent a representative to negotiate, they should ask the Shantou branch director to handle the matter. In reality, although Shen was a director, his family's financial situation was also quite poor.

Bandits Conduct Secret Investigation

When the bandits allowed the three men to send letters home, the bandit leader immediately sent his accomplices to investigate the financial situation of the three hostages, to determine if they had any assets, which would be used to set the ransom price. The three letters also mentioned that the bandits had sent people to conduct a secret investigation into the family circumstances of each person. However, how the investigation was being conducted was unknown.

Inventor of Writing Cloth Received Assistance from Municipal Chamber of Commerce 113

Public Experiment Very Satisfactory

Writing cloth, needed by the Chinese cultural community, has always been imported, resulting in significant financial outflow each year. Zhu Jun Shilie devoted himself to research to counter this. However, due to financial constraints, he had not yet been able to establish a factory. After the newspapers reported on this, many people from all walks of life visited Zhu Jun's residence to see his work. Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, after receiving a letter from Zhu Jun requesting assistance, sent Mr. Xue Jianxin to Zhu's residence to investigate and conduct a face-to-face experiment. The results were excellent, and they promised substantial assistance. The following is a record of Zhu Jun's research process. Zhu Jun has a keen interest in scientific research. Ten years ago, he founded the Scientific Research Association, initially producing building steel tools and other items. Due to the failure of the Shanghai war, he turned his attention to chemistry, researching day and night with tireless efforts. Later, Sun Siyi, a reporter for the Financial Western News, proposed researching the invention of writing cloth. He spent two years but was unsuccessful, and his personal finances and spirit were on the verge of collapse. Fortunately, Mr. Sun repeatedly encouraged him and provided financial support, so he did not give up. After repeated experiments and painstaking exploration, he finally succeeded. He sent samples to major bookstores for testing, proving that they were superior to foreign products. However, he was unfamiliar with the procedures for registering with the Ministry of Industry and requesting rewards. Therefore, he wrote to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce for assistance. Yesterday, the chamber sent representative Xue Jianxin to Zhu Jun's residence at No. 3 Renhuai Lane, Xicang Street, in the city to conduct an on-site inspection and investigate whether it was entirely made of domestic raw materials. Zhu Jun personally presented the manufacturing chemical formula and publicly tested the manufacturing methods for writing cloth, such as imitation leather, crepe cloth, and lacquered cloth. The results were very satisfactory to Mr. Xue, and he agreed to submit a report. The chamber will do its best to assist in requesting the Ministry of Industry to grant rewards and exclusive manufacturing rights.

Yesterday morning, Tang, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Wei and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the scene. After examining the body, Western police chief Wei A reported the situation and said that he had notified the family the day before yesterday that they should come to claim the body the next morning, but they had not yet arrived and requested instructions. Tang said that the examination showed that the deceased, Feng Liu Shi, was a female who died from opium poisoning. The family had not yet arrived, so the body was temporarily handed over to the Pushan Villa for safekeeping. It was later learned that the reason the deceased's mother-in-law and husband had not arrived at the autopsy room was that they were trying to borrow money for a coffin.

Record of Autopsy of Eleven Poisoning Deaths

One After Another, Poisoned Victims Die in Hospital, En Route, and at Friends' Homes 118

Collect Remaining Food, Postpone Coffin Closure, and Re-Test or Autopsy

The Shunxing Restaurant at 50 Rue Orloff, Hongkou, suffered an incident the day before yesterday in which diners died from poisoning. The restaurant is owned by Han Huatang and Lin Rongzeng (44 years old, residing at 28 Dongbaoxing Road) from Haimen, and Li Zitang (46 years old, residing at 31 Sanle Lane, Xingjiaqiao Road). The restaurant specializes in providing food for laborers. All the food is taken from leftover food from major restaurants, re-cooked, and resold at low prices. The victims, mostly rickshaw pullers and laborers, ate the third batch of rice of the day before becoming ill. A total of eleven died. Two died on the spot: Gu Koulang, from Chongming, residing at 147 Fengtian Road, and Chen Ziying, 41 years old. Zhou Da Erzi collapsed and died on Linping Road while on his way home. Lu Jiayu, 30 years old, from Yancheng, residing at 8 Liancheng Lane, Tiantong Road; Jiang Xiaogenzi, 19 years old; Ding Fushan, 47 years old, both rickshaw pullers, residing in Oujiacun, Hongsheng Lane, Rue Orloff; and Luo Mingkui (also known as Honglin), 57 years old, former police chief of the North Sichuan Road branch, all died at home. Zhao Xiaolao Hai, 19 years old, from Yancheng, residing in a grass hut on Linping Road; Ma Kuijin, 25 years old, residing at 45 Ruihua Lane, Rue Orloff; and Xu Zhenhong, 35 years old, residing at 7 Gongkuan Lane, Yucai Road, all died at Tongren Hospital before they could be treated. Cao Zhenhai (also known as Ai Qiang), a local, 26 years old, residing at 59 Rue Orloff, had visited a friend on Yangjiabang Road after the meal, so he died at his friend's house before he could be treated. The incident was not noticed at the time. The authorities were first reported to the Linping Road branch, and the restaurant owners, except for Han Huatang who escaped, have been successively detained by the Linping Road branch. These include Lin Rongzeng, Li Zitang, Yin Tianmu (43 years old, from Zhenjiang), Li Caigen (40 years old, from Haimen) and Lu Caixiang (32 years old). The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau has paid close attention to this incident and has delegated the Director of the Testing Institute and chemists to investigate. They have collected leftover food and fish bones in the garbage can for testing. The results have not been determined yet. All bodies, except Cao Zhenhai who was reported too late for verification, were reported to the local court yesterday morning. The court then delegated prosecutor Wu Deying and a team of examiners to conduct an investigation yesterday afternoon. As the cause of poisoning is unclear, the local heads were ordered to arrange for preliminary burial of the bodies without closing the coffins and wait for a re-examination or autopsy. At the same time, the Linping Road Public Security Bureau was instructed to transfer the leftovers to the court and send them to the Zhenru Forensic Examination Institute for examination. It is believed that an autopsy will be required.

Railways Still Responsible for Transporting Easily Damaged Goods 119

The Joint Transportation Department of the Ministry of Railways sent a letter to the two road management offices stating that, according to the 50th proposal of the 17th National Joint Transportation Conference, easily damaged goods such as glass should still be the responsibility of the railway if they are transported as parcels. The proposal was decided upon in the 130th resolution. The Joint Transportation Department sent a letter to the various joint transportation routes regarding the packaging of easily damaged goods. The letter stated that detailed inspection should be conducted during consignment and special labels should be affixed to ensure careful handling during loading and unloading. In addition to sending separate letters, we are informing you to check and handle accordingly. The bureau has instructed the traffic department to comply.

City Chamber of Commerce to Hold Exhibition of Improved Chinese Bookkeeping Starting Tomorrow 120

From the 1st to the 3rd

From 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM

Our country's current bookkeeping is broadly divided into two schools: Chinese and Western. Western bookkeeping uses a horizontal format, and the paper, ink, accounting principles, and methods all rely on foreign imports. Not only is it difficult to imitate, but the cost is also enormous. Chinese bookkeeping uses a vertical format, and the paper, ink, accounting principles, and methods are all familiar to Chinese people. However, the system is flawed, lacks organization, and fails to meet the fundamental purpose of accounting, so it is often criticized. Mr. Xu Yongzuo, an accountant in this city, has spent more than ten years researching and compiling more than forty kinds of improved Chinese accounting books and forms. Each type is accompanied by detailed explanations, and a book entitled "An Overview of Improved Chinese Bookkeeping" has also been compiled to provide a general explanation of the entire improvement plan. Since its publication last year, it has attracted considerable attention throughout the country. The City Chamber of Commerce has held large-scale lectures and exhibitions for it. The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce and the Chinese Institute of Accounting Policy have also sent separate letters of introduction. Major newspapers in this city have successively published special issues on improved Chinese bookkeeping, demonstrating the importance attached to it by society. This year, more and more people are adopting improved Chinese bookkeeping, and its effectiveness is becoming increasingly apparent. The City Chamber of Commerce and Mr. Xu's accounting firm are also constantly engaged in training bookkeeping personnel and promoting the improvement plan. The Chamber of Commerce will hold a large-scale achievement exhibition at its premises from the 1st of next month to February. The details are as follows:

Training Process　Since the exhibition and lectures on improved Chinese bookkeeping were held last year, requests for opening training courses to train bookkeeping personnel have been overwhelming. Remote areas such as Shaanxi, Sichuan, Guangdong, Guangxi, and the South Seas Islands, as well as nearby areas such as Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shandong, Jiangxi, and Anhui, often send letters requesting correspondence courses. Mr. Xu, Mr. Wang Yansong, Standing Committee Member of the City Chamber of Commerce and Principal of the Commercial Night School, and Mr. Yan Esheng, Secretary of the City Chamber of Commerce and Deputy Principal of the Commercial Night School, jointly drafted a simple charter and prepared a statement of purpose. The Commercial Night School of the City Chamber of Commerce and Xu Yongzuo Accounting Tutorial School jointly established an improved Chinese bookkeeping training course. Enrollment began on the 10th of July, with a planned enrollment of 400 students. However, the number of applicants was extremely enthusiastic, exceeding 700 in less than ten days. Later, there were hundreds more who could not be accommodated. Classes began on August 1st, with one hour of instruction each morning. Mr. Xu Yongzuo served as the chief instructor, and Mr. Pan Shihao, Mr. Xu Hanqing, Mr. Zhang Jun, and Mr. Lu Shanzhi served as instructors. The term was two months, with systematic explanations of improved Chinese bookkeeping and practical exercises on various accounting books and forms. In addition, special lectures were given by Mr. Wang Yansong, Mr. Yan Esheng, and Mr. Xu Yongzuo during weekend breaks. The classroom was located in the assembly hall of the City Chamber of Commerce. Due to the large number of people, the China Wireless Radio Research Institute installed a public lecture machine to facilitate listening. Lectures were completed on September 30th, and the instructors continued to guide the students in practical exercises. Graduation exams were held in late October. Recently, the examination of all academic achievements was completed. A total of 427 graduates passed, with 95 in Grade A, 164 in Grade B, and 160 in Grade C. Most of them are accounting personnel in the industrial and commercial sectors. Graduation certificates were issued on the previous two days. This is the first large-scale training of accounting personnel in the domestic business community.

Continued Promotion　Since the end of the improved Chinese bookkeeping training course, there have been many requests from all walks of life to continue the course, and many requests from other places for correspondence courses. Mr. Xu Yongzuo started a correspondence course in October, and the number of students has reached more than 590. At the same time, he jointly runs an elective course on improved Chinese bookkeeping with the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, and a specialized course on improved Chinese bookkeeping with the Shanghai Machinery-Made National Goods Factory Union. Mr. Pan Shihao, an employee of Xu's accounting firm, serves as the instructor. All the courses are roughly the same as the training course, but the Machinery Union focuses on manufacturing bookkeeping. Most of the students are accounting personnel from various factories. They are currently engaged in practical exercises on various accounting books and forms, and are expected to graduate around the end of the year. According to officials from the Machinery Union, various factories have a good impression of improved Chinese bookkeeping and plan to adopt it in batches after the graduation of this year's students to see its practical effects.

Achievement Exhibition　During the training period of the improved Chinese bookkeeping course, students have practiced various accounting books and forms many times. Many of the practical exercise papers are excellent and can be used as a reference for those who adopt improved Chinese bookkeeping. Mr. Xu's newly revised improved accounting books and explanatory books are also suitable for publication at this time. Therefore, the City Chamber of Commerce and Mr. Xu agreed that from December 1st to 3rd, the best student achievements will be selected for exhibition at the City Chamber of Commerce for three days. Each day, from 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM, all sectors are welcome to visit and view freely. At the same time, more than forty kinds of improved Chinese accounting books and forms recently published by the Standard Accounting Form Document Manufacturing Institute, as well as the newly revised sixth edition of the "Overview of Improved Chinese Bookkeeping" and lecture notes, will be displayed for comparison. During the exhibition, many graduates of the training course will provide guidance and explanations to visitors. At 10:00 AM on the 2nd, a lecture will be held to elaborate on various issues related to improved Chinese bookkeeping. Mr. Xu Yongzuo, an accountant, and prominent figures from the business community will personally give lectures. It is reported that the City Chamber of Commerce has sent letters to all trade associations, informing all members to participate.

Trial of Shanghai Bank Robbery Case 123

At about 9:00 AM on the 21st of this month, the Shanghai Bank sent 5,200 yuan to the savings office of Jiaotong University on Haig Road. On the way, it was robbed. Yang Peisheng, the Chinese detective chief of the Yulin Road Police Station, along with detectives Huang Yufu and Ma Wenda, arrested the criminals Tan Jingeng, Huang Yaosheng, Zhang Zilong, and Liu Yucai. Zhang Yuanyuan from Haimen and Zhu Xuelong, a tea servant at Jiaotong University, were subsequently arrested in the jurisdiction of the Sixth District of Zhabei. Tan Jingeng and others were detained in the Public Security Bureau and escorted to the First Special District Court for interrogation. All of this has been reported in this newspaper. The Chinese and Western detectives in charge of this case subsequently arrested Fei Amei, a local accomplice, at No. 4 Qingxue Road in Zhabei. Together with the Zhang and Zhu criminals, they were brought back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, Li Zhishan, the lawyer of the Public Works Department, detailed the process to the Third Criminal Court and requested an extension for a joint trial. Fei Amei confessed that Xuegen, who is at large, invited him to Zhang Zilong's house on Daxilu to discuss the robbery. After the incident, he received 150 yuan. Zhang Ruiyuan confessed that Zhang Zilong is his cousin, denied going to the robbery, and only got two yuan. Zhu Xuelong confessed that he delivered documents at Jiaotong University. Because the bank delivered money every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday, he informed Zhang Zilong a month ago. Afterwards, he received 230 yuan. Judge Xiao Xiefen ordered them to be remanded in custody and rescheduled for a joint trial with Tan Jingeng and others.

Resolution of Rickshaw Dispute Case 124

The Vehicle Committee Gave a Satisfactory Reply to All Rickshaw Merchants

Rickshaw Owners Form Repair and Manufacturing Cooperative

Various disputes over rickshaw replacement, etc. in the Special District have been resolved through negotiations between the rickshaw merchants and the Vehicle Committee, and have been approved by the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department. The details have been recorded by the reporter of Xin Sheng News Agency from the Public Works Department as follows:

Rickshaw Merchants' Request　Rickshaw merchants in the Special District have repeatedly sent representatives, Yin Zhiling and Gu Songmao, to negotiate with the Vehicle Committee regarding rickshaw registration and replacement, and have put forward the following requests: (1) For the registration of public rickshaw pullers, in addition to the regulations for the registration of private rickshaw pullers, the rickshaw owners should introduce them. (2) The rickshaw owners' existing old-style new rickshaws should be allowed to be inspected and stamped from now on for continued use. (3) In order to facilitate and assist rickshaw owners in continuously replacing new-style vehicles, the vehicles may be mortgaged. (4) After the implementation of the new rickshaws, the vehicle inspection should be changed from once every two months to once every six months. (5) In addition to complying with the agreement on rickshaw rent of 1.50 yuan per day on August 6, the rickshaw companies should be allowed to collect arrears, savings, and accommodation fees from the rickshaw pullers.

Vehicle Committee's Reply　The Vehicle Committee replied: (1) The registration of public rickshaw pullers will be carried out according to the method of registering private rickshaw pullers. The decision of 30,000 people should be introduced by the rickshaw owners. If it can proceed smoothly, the Committee will be responsible for considering and will sympathetically suggest to the Public Works Department that the rickshaw owners introduce the remaining rickshaw pullers for registration. If the registration reaches 40,000 people and it is still not enough to allocate, the Committee is prepared to increase the number of registered places. Only when the registered rickshaw pullers meet the required number of people can the registered rickshaw pullers be allowed to pull rickshaws. If the registered rickshaw puller is proven to have violated regulations and the license is revoked, or due to death, permanent departure from Shanghai, or bad behavior, the Committee will allow the rickshaw owner to introduce a replacement rickshaw puller. (2) In order to take into account the difficulties of the rickshaw merchants, if they are willing to actively cooperate in the rickshaw puller registration procedures, the Committee will suggest to the Public Works Department that 350 vehicles be replaced with vehicles that are no longer usable. The replacement of old-style new rickshaws should not affect the vehicles that have already been ordered to be replaced with new-style vehicles or have their licenses revoked. The extension for the replacement of the 231 vehicles that have already been ordered to be replaced will be extended by one month. The materials for the new-style vehicles can be modified, and the rickshaw owners can freely make suggestions. The Committee will adopt suggestions that are found to be beneficial. The new chapter of spraying paint can be replaced with various types of top-grade paint. (3) The Committee hereby reiterates that the Public Works Department has no intention of interfering with the mortgage of vehicles. If the mortgagee goes through formal and legal procedures to transfer the vehicle, and has sufficient evidence and the original owner's certificate, the transfer of the certificate will be approved. The Public Works Department Gazette of August 10th published the following Article 9 of the agreement between the Public Works Department representatives and the rickshaw owners on August 6th: "In order to resolve the ambiguity and misunderstanding in the wording of the public rickshaw license rules, two items have been agreed as follows: (A) The rickshaw owner who obtains the vehicle license does not have to be an individual, but the rickshaw company or guild can be the licensee. (B) Although the Bureau reserves the right to approve or disapprove the issuance of licenses at the end of each month, it will give considerable convenience to the transfer of vehicles due to sale or the transfer due to the death of the licensee. If the new licensee is deemed to be a suitable person and is willing to abide by the license rules and pay the rickshaw puller mutual aid fund donations, then the Bureau will approve the application when they purchase the vehicle or inherit it according to law." Of course, it can also be applied to mortgaged vehicles. (4) In order to meet the requirements of the rickshaw owners, the Committee will try to grant special permission for new-style vehicles to be inspected once every four months instead of once every two months. If this inspection method is satisfactory after the trial, the Committee will continue to implement it. The Committee is currently unwilling to cancel the licenses of rickshaws that are not in good condition, but is willing to try to first warn the rickshaw owners to improve new-style vehicles if there are any dissatisfaction and temporarily not

Cancelling the license. Rickshaw owners can apply to the Committee for a substitute worker's license badge if they automatically repair the vehicles. However, the license for the vehicle under repair should be deposited with the Public Works Department during the business hours of the substitute rickshaw. (5) Inquiring about the first item agreed upon by the rickshaw merchant representatives and the Public Works Department on August 6th, the daily rickshaw rent for public rickshaws from August 15th of this year will be a maximum of 0.78 yuan. Rickshaw owners who have prepaid the rickshaw puller mutual aid fund donation of 1.50 silver coins per vehicle per month may collect an additional

Seven cents per vehicle per day from the rickshaw puller in addition to the rickshaw rent. It is of course legal for the rickshaw company to collect arrears, savings, and accommodation fees from the rickshaw pullers. However, a receipt must be given for the collection of money and the rickshaw rent must be accounted for separately. If the rickshaw puller has an obligation to pay this amount, a separate account book should be kept for the Committee to check.　　Establishing a Cooperative　The requirements and replies of both parties have been approved by the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department, and all disputes have been resolved. The rickshaw merchants also held a meeting and decided to establish a rickshaw repair and manufacturing cooperative. The intention is to purchase all of the more than 1,000 new rickshaw shells stored in the rickshaw company. Those approved for use by the Vehicle Committee will then be sold by the cooperative to replace the 131 new-style rickshaws. The replacement of new-style vehicles will also be undertaken by the cooperative and sold to the rickshaw owners. The cooperative's handling fees will be distributed and raised equally among the rickshaw owners. It is purely a cooperation of the same industry to equalize the economic burden of the rickshaw merchants. The principle has been approved by the meeting and will be convened again to establish it.

Verdict of Mei Hua Company Sued Case 127

Pronouncement Tomorrow Afternoon

Pan Wenxia, a female actress from Nanjing of Mei Hua Film Company, was previously sued by the company's manager Zhu Ruifeng and Tang Hao lawyer for breach of trust at the First Special Court because she went to Shanghai Film Company to shoot a film during working hours without the company's permission. Later, the case was withdrawn after a settlement. However, the prosecutor's office of the Special Court, because there were many rumors outside that this prosecution actually contained the use of the court as a propaganda machine, and there were many doubts in the whole case, so the prosecutor Zhong Qing filed a public prosecution against Zhu Ruifeng and Tang Hao in accordance with Article 180 of the Criminal Law. The relevant information has been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zehan opened the Second Criminal Court for interrogation. Zhu hired lawyer Tan Yigong and Tang hired lawyers Dong Kang and Shi Liang for defense. Prosecutor Zhong Chen stated the intention of the prosecution, saying that the Ministry of Justice's Order No. 233 stipulated that civil cases filed with criminal charges should be treated as false accusations. Now, Zhu Ruifeng's case against Pan Wenxia is clearly a civil breach of contract case, but it is criminally prosecuted, which is actually a false accusation. It should be judged according to law.

Zhu Ruifeng confessed that Pan's incident was actually a breach of trust, so I entrusted lawyer Tang Hao to file a lawsuit. It was my intention at the time. Tang Hao confessed that this case was entrusted by Zhu. After he stated the facts, he wanted to file a lawsuit for breach of trust. After considering it, I believed that Pan's behavior met the conditions for breach of trust, so I drafted a lawsuit on behalf of the party according to the party's wishes. Then, the court ordered the start of the debate. After the prosecutor Zhong and the defendant's defense lawyer debated each other, Judge Wu ruled that the debate was over and the verdict was scheduled to be announced on the afternoon of December 1.

Yongde Pawnshop Robbed 129

Yongde Pawnshop on Hujiamuqiao Road in this city has been established for many years. Next door is a Tingshunlong Iron Shop opened by Ding Amei from Wuxi. At about 10:00 PM the other night, the workers of the iron shop were about to go to bed because they had worked too hard during the day. Suddenly, seven bandits broke into the door. The leader took out a pistol from his waist and said that no noise was allowed. The other bandits used iron tools to make a big hole in the wall and put a quilt on the ground to prevent the bricks and stones from making noise when they fell. They laughed in their mouths. The next door, in the middle of a sweet dream, thought that the neighbor was disturbing them and that nothing unexpected had happened. When the bandits came out of the hole and broke into the room, they woke up from their dreams. The bandits took out their guns to stop them from shouting, forced them to open the cabinet to get money, and searched everywhere. They robbed more than 280 yuan in cash and valuables such as gold rings and jewelry, worth about 500 or 600 yuan. When the bandits saw that their goal had been achieved, they left. Afterwards, the owner of the shop reported the details of the robbery to the Jiaxing Road Police Station. Chinese and Western detectives went to investigate. Weather Report 136

The Xujiahui Observatory issued a weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday, saying that Shandong is cloudy and cold all around, with northwest to northeast winds of varying degrees. The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy and chilly, with gentle winds from the north to the east. There is fog in the East China Sea and the Taiwan Strait in the morning, the sky is overcast, and there is local rain. The northeast wind is quite strong. A hurricane will pass Chaiyasi Island and move west-northwest. Its center moved to within 60 miles of 12 degrees north latitude and 125 degrees east longitude at 6:00 AM. The wind force is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 54.9 and the lowest was 37.8. On the same day last year, the highest was 63.9 and the lowest was 43.5.

Educational News

Qi University Has Resumed Classes 137

After Director He of the Department of Education Strongly Urged

(Jinan, 28th) All students of the College of Arts and Sciences of Qi University went to the Provincial Government to petition this morning. Director He Siyuan of the Department of Education received them on behalf of the government and tried to maintain order. He advised the students to return to school to resume classes, and he was responsible for contacting the Board of Directors by letter. He also stated that if the Board of Directors does not adopt the government's opinions, the government will not be responsible for anything that happens to the school in the future. Classes resumed this afternoon.

Declaration of the Students of the College of Arts and Sciences of Qi University on Suspending Classes to Promote the Resolution of School Affairs.

Since President Zhu Jingnong resigned in the summer of the 21st year of the Republic of China, the Board of Directors has not produced a formal president. Only Mr. Lin Jiqing, Dean of the College of Arts and Sciences, has temporarily served as an agent. In the past two years, Agent Lin has worked hard to manage the school, and he has been assisted by the local government. The reputation of Qi University has been rising. Anyone who is interested can tell. Therefore, on August 15 this year, the Board of Directors formally passed a resolution to ask Mr. Lin to become the formal president in order to facilitate the development of school affairs. However, the Westerner Wei Limu, Shi Duoma, and others on the board were instigated by Dr. Schilder, Dean of the Medical School, and had ulterior motives. They intended to destroy the existence of our College of Arts and Sciences. After the resolution was passed, they repeatedly obstructed it. Seeing that the future was difficult, Mr. Lin resigned angrily at the beginning of this semester. Minister Kong Xiangxi also resigned as Chairman of the Board. The Board of Directors considered the issue to be serious, so it resolved on October 5 to send three representatives to the south to retain Kong and Lin, and the representatives also visited the local authorities and Mayor Shen to ask for assistance in retaining them. This time, Chairman Kong passed through Lu on official business and was repeatedly urged by the local officials to agree to withdraw his resignation and continue to be responsible. However, Wei Limu, Schilder, and others still insisted on their private opinions and acted arbitrarily. They manipulated everything in this Board of Directors meeting, forcing the Chinese directors to withdraw, and illegally overturned the resolution of August 15 with four votes (all Westerners, and not enough for a quorum). As a result, the list of students could not be submitted to the Ministry of Education, and the public was in an uproar. The students felt that the urgent solution to their own problems and the illegal manipulation of the Western directors had unimaginable consequences. Therefore, on November 20, the entire group gathered to petition the four Western directors, requesting them to abandon all private opinions and focus on the future of the school and the studies of all students, and on the one hand, they continued to attend classes as usual. The reason why the students did this was to take care of their own studies and were unwilling to take strike action to form a serious situation. We hope that all circles will understand this humble heart. Unexpectedly, Wei Limu and others regarded the students as insulting and had no sincerity in accepting the opinions of the whole group. They also made improper remarks and arbitrarily insulted them. In the end, due to the situation, they agreed to submit this issue to the entire Board of Directors for resolution. The students have lost trust in the repeated changes of Wei Limu and others. Even if the entire Board of Directors is convened, whether this Board of Directors can not be manipulated by them, whether the resolutions passed can not be obstructed by them, whether the president produced will be beneficial to our College of Arts and Sciences, all of these are questionable. Wei and others' actions are by no means sincere, but another insidious means to implement their destruction of our College of Arts and Sciences. This is undoubtedly the case. Therefore, the current dispute in our school is by no means a simple issue of the president, but an issue of Chinese people and two or three Western directors fighting for educational rights. The students should attach importance to their studies, which goes without saying. However, they are determined to oppose the use of education as a tool for personal fame and profit by Wei and others. Therefore, all students decided to reluctantly suspend classes from November 26, hoping to promote their awareness and petition the local officials for assistance. The matter was out of desperation, and the abandonment of studies is the responsibility of Wei and others. This has to be solemnly stated. Although the students are in a church school, they are receiving Chinese education and will definitely oppose all evil forces that destroy our Chinese education with all their strength. All our Chinese people should have sympathy. However, the students have limited ability, and the success or failure is of great importance. We hope that our Chinese people will give them voice so that they can achieve their ultimate goal. Then Chinese education will be fortunate, and all students of our College of Arts and Sciences will be fortunate.

According to a letter from the students of the Medical School of Qi University, the Medical School did not participate in the strike.

The matters to be carried out were (1) to send a letter to the Guangzhao Guild Hall to request the placement of the students who lost their studies. If there is no satisfactory reply, all the students will go to petition. (2) To write to the Cantonese overseas Chinese groups to appeal, and at the same time, advertise to the fellow villagers in Shanghai. (3) To submit a letter to the party, government, and educational authorities for help. The temporary office of the support association is located at No. 21, Lane 76, Dengtuo Road.

This Week's Individual Sports Meet 157

Saturday | High Jump, Pole Vault

Sunday | Jiangwan Cross-Country Run

Next Week: Men's and Women's Race Walking

Individual sports are extremely popular, but because the association's members are required to pay a membership fee of twenty cents, it has led to misunderstandings from the outside, mistaking it for a registration fee, which is not accurate. The association's monthly income and expenditure statements are compiled into reports and distributed to each member, and there is a full-time staff responsible, supervised by all the initiators. There is absolutely no possibility of profiteering. The association is scheduled to hold men's and women's Group A and B high jump competitions, men's Group A and B pole vault competitions, and women's 50-meter Group A and B competitions at the City No. 1 Sports Field starting at 1:30 PM this Saturday. Little Western Paradise 167

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 5: Fawning Smiles Meet the Lamp's Light; Wan and Haggard, Driven by Hungry Stomach, Applying Powder and Learning Flirtatiousness

When that Sister Hu was talking to you, I heard it from the side. After your husband left, I complained to him, saying he had eyes but didn't recognize Mount Tai [didn't recognize a great person]. He said he didn't mean to contradict Master Jia on purpose. Because he was in front of so many people, Master Jia said several things to him. If he didn't talk back, he was afraid people would laugh at him. Jia Duocai said: "He shouldn't have contradicted me even more in front of people." Xiao Ji said, "Yes, that's what I said too. Moreover, what the masters say always has a reason. He should have thought before answering." Let me point it out to him, and he'll understand. He said he would come tomorrow to apologize to Master Jia. Jia Duocai said: "What a joke! Don't come. Am I going to argue about right and wrong with this kind of person?" Xiao Ji lightly said: "It's not just him coming alone. He's bringing that little girl too." Jia Duocai couldn't help but laugh at this, and said: "That's even more wrong. That little girl didn't offend me. Why should she come to apologize?" Xiao Ji laughed: "That's just what I'm saying. Isn't Master Jia clear about what's in his heart?" Jia Duocai laughed: "Let me tell you, you've got the wrong idea. You think I'm from the bank, so I must have money. You don't know, the bank is opened by other people. I just work at the bank." Xiao Ji laughed: "Master Jia, we can't afford you to say that. I dared to say this because I saw that Master Jia really liked that girl. If you didn't have any feelings for her, then we would be setting a trap to cheat you out of money." Jia Duocai saw that Zhu Yueying wasn't with Li Shilian, and this was completely his own misunderstanding. He already quite understood Hu Saozi. Now that he heard that Zhu Yueying would come to apologize, he felt even more moved. So he laughed: "If they really want to

come, I can't stop them. But when there are a lot of people, tell them not to come. If they come, they should come quietly." Xiao Ji said: "Please let Master Jia decide on a time himself." Jia Duocai took out a cigarette case from his pocket, took out a cigarette, and sat in a chair, tilting his head to smoke. (77)

In Memory of Mr. Shi Liangcai 168

— Chen Zhuzun

Tears fall frequently all day long. Not crying for Mr. Shi. Not crying, yet crying. What kind of feeling is this? (Mr. Shi's achievements are in society, dying unnaturally. What is lost is not just one person. Therefore, what I mourn today is not just Mr. Shi.) Who said the world is wide? Not allowing righteous people to walk. Who said the world is narrow? Demons and monsters follow closely. I remember last summer. Taking my child to knock on your door. A long talk of an hour. Loving words of dingning (careful instructions). (This summer, my child returned from the United States. Mr. Zhao Housheng introduced him to Mr. Shi. He also invited me to go with them. Upon seeing my child, Mr. Shi immediately expected him to be great and decided to extend an invitation to the Shen Bao newspaper office. Later, my child changed his mind and accepted appointments from Guanghua and Datong universities. Whenever I think of this, I often feel regret.) Unexpectedly, within a few months. Suddenly returning to the dark depths. Where can I find a demon-revealing mirror? To see the shapes of all the monsters. Where can I find a pair of flying dragons? To clear the way for you.

Tidbits 169

Mr. (Someone) was also a sociable figure in society. However, he had a peculiar habit. The Ethereal Record of Imperial Fragrance 170

— Originally Written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

Let's suppose that, halfway through her tour, she suddenly thought of an important military and national matter, and wanted to write an imperial decree immediately, then pens, ink, paper, and inkstones would be delivered to her immediately. Furthermore, if her hair was blown by the wind, and she wanted to quickly tidy it up, she only needed to wave her hand or say a word. Her hairdresser, who was also a eunuch and greatly trusted by the Empress Dowager (she praised him as the number one hairdresser in China), would immediately bring the necessary tools and come to serve her. As for towels, fragrant powders, and other various cosmetics, they were even more readily available, easily obtained at any time and any place.

"There are four palaces here that we must visit." The Empress Dowager suddenly spoke to us during the procession. She was speaking to everyone, but I always felt that she was speaking to me alone. Although I knew this was just wishful thinking, I truly hoped so in my heart. Because I remembered very clearly that she had repeatedly told me that, once she passed away, the only person who could tell the world about her personality, character, behavior, and all aspects of her daily private life was me. Therefore, she wanted me to understand all the truths and realities, so that I would not be as isolated and misunderstood as outsiders. Her hope for me was that I would tell what I actually saw in the future, without adding or subtracting anything. At that time, she continued to explain to us why those four palaces could not be missed. "What is stored inside are the relics left by our Qing Dynasty emperors!"

She indeed led us into those four palaces, so we knew that they contained the relics of eight generations of emperors. Originally, this Guangxu Emperor, a political prisoner, was already the ninth emperor of the Qing Dynasty after entering the Pass. (187)

Country Bumpkin 171

— Yang Yusheng

I also echoed the slogan "Go to the countryside" — and I was originally from the countryside. But my footsteps rarely step on "native land." So when someone from the countryside comes to Shanghai to see me, I feel extraordinarily cordial.

"Calculating" is an unbreakable habit of country people. I often warn them that Shanghai is not like the countryside and they must not be calculating. But they actually learn the trick of sitting on the "oil train" [illegally riding the tram], and the result is often being ordered to leave by the ticket inspector, and running back with sore legs!

They seem to know that Shanghai is where "pickpockets" come from, and that pickpockets are sure to pick on country people, so they dare not carry much money when they go out. Even the "tram copper coins" have to be carefully budgeted, just enough to cover the round-trip fare. If they want to buy some things and stroll on the street, their silver dollars must be carefully wrapped in layers of straw paper and newspaper before putting them into the bottom of the "belly band" worn in front of their lower abdomen. If they encounter a guy with a crooked hat and greasy hair on the tram, and they feel like a hand is groping at their belly band, they have to make a great determination to get off the tram quickly, find a quiet place with "urine stains" and let loose a bubble of urine to check if anything has been stolen -

Speaking of their "belly band," I always call it the "Cosmos Sack." Needless to say, silver dollars, deeds to land, pawn tickets, tobacco boxes, lighters, medicine bottles, and eyeglass cases all have to squeeze inside to join the fun. Therefore, when country people buy something and dig out their wallets from the Cosmos Sack, opening the layers of wrapping, the time and effort it takes is enough to annoy the shopkeeper -

They are mostly followers of Roosevelt, advocating the "silver policy" and not very fond of banknotes. They also have good reason. It is said that bringing silver dollars into a gambling den, even if you lose, you won't be ruined, because you can't bear to bet heavily with silver, unlike banknotes, which are thrown out in tens of dollars without feeling the pain - and each silver dollar has 7.2 fen of silver. Fifty of them stacked up are five inches long, which is much better for "admiring" than banknotes, especially since the latter sometimes run the risk of becoming "fake money"!

The Terror of the God of Peace 172

— Tong Fu

Radio Announcer 173

— Zhu Ying

Since radios have become prized possessions in most upper-class families, the broadcasting industry has seen tremendous growth. At the same time, the production of song and dance troupes has become a case of demand exceeding supply, although dance is absolutely unnecessary in the broadcast studio. Thus, becoming a radio announcer has become a great career path for most female graduates of today's schools, because any broadcast song and dance troupe needs several female members with melodious voices.

Being a radio announcer is naturally better than being a dancer who is hugged by people, better than being a film actress who is played with by male actors, and even better than being a female employee who is treated as a beautiful vase. Because when you are a radio announcer, you only need to sing two or three songs in the broadcast studio. You don't show your body, you only show your face, and you won't be harassed by frivolous playboys. At the same time, the reward is better than that of those who bare their legs and perform grass skirt dances. Therefore, many ladies from well-to-do families have now joined song and dance troupes and become radio announcers.

But even so, being a radio announcer does not necessarily mean that you can avoid bad environments. Especially if you become a popular radio announcer, you will be tempted even more. I have a relative's daughter who is a radio announcer in a certain song and dance troupe. It is said that she receives at least ten love letters every day, and some even call to ask her to go to the movies or have a big meal. She replies to each love letter with a pre-printed letter. As for those who ask her to go out, regardless of whether she knows them or not, she always agrees, but when she goes, she always asks at least three or five companions to go with her, so that the frivolous ones cannot tempt her after paying for the guests.

Little Gardening

Brief Notes on Planting Chrysanthemums 174

— Xin Ren

As soon as the season reaches autumn, there is a vague feeling of emptiness in my heart. Living in this city of only yellow sand and smoky ash, besides some material displays, to find a single green leaf as a consolation from nature is like searching for sweet water in a desert. So, the thought of finding some flowers and plants to grow myself, to make up for this deficiency, has long been present. However, after several attempts, it was almost always a case of "repeated failures." Having learned a lesson, I knew that without empty space or time, it was better not to plant flowers, lest the little lives sprout only to wither away in solitude. Recently, however, I moved, and next to the house, I actually discovered a vacant plot more than two feet square. Looking closer, the soil was still fertile and dark. So, seized by a sudden impulse, I wanted to try my hand again at planting some flowers and plants, and the first thing I thought of was chrysanthemums. I went to the market, where there were fully grown chrysanthemums for sale. Sowing seeds was already out of season, and I was too lazy to wait for the seeds to sprout and gradually grow. So, the fully grown chrysanthemums in the market suited my intention perfectly. I bought several plants with many buds and happily skipped back home, like a child who had received a lovely toy.

My wife, who also loves flowers and plants, gave me a sarcastic remark when she saw me carrying several chrysanthemums back: "You fool!" For a moment, I didn't understand the meaning of "fool." I stared at her for a while, and then she said, as if explaining: "Oh! Some wild chrysanthemums, what kind of famous varieties are they?" But then she added: "Chrysanthemums will wither, I want a flower that won't wither."

"Where in the world is there a flower that doesn't wither? It's like there are no people who don't age," I said.

"Look!" my wife said, pointing with a smile at the mirror, next to which were inserted paper flowers she had made herself. "Aren't those flowers that won't wither?" At this moment, I couldn't help but laugh at my wife's foolishness. Because handmade paper flowers, not being real flowers, are like bronze or plaster statues, not being real people, are fake. At the same time, fake flowers and fake human figures are only a kind of longing and remembrance for the real thing, not a real existence. It is precisely because flowers wither that the value of flowers is revealed. Don't we feel the fleeting nature of youth and the urgency of life? I said to my wife, "Let's plant them together, you are truly foolish."

After planting the several chrysanthemums, I felt as if I had added a lot of busyness to my heart. Every day, as soon as I opened my eyes, I would go and see how much the chrysanthemums had grown? Whether they had more vitality than when I bought them? Every evening, I would also water them, and sometimes I would go with my wife to look at the buds, predicting the day they would bloom. Therefore, the joy I gained from these leaves every day was truly not something that could be bought with the money spent on purchasing them. I could even imagine that a gardener in a flower garden would have to worry much more than the owner of a flower garden, but also get much more pleasure from the flowers.

But half a month passed, and the chrysanthemums were still no different from when I bought them. At first, I thought that because I met with the chrysanthemums every day, it was not easy to see the difference. So, I decided to look at them every two days. Looking at the chrysanthemums every two days, they were still the same. And two of them looked like they were about to die. Naturally, I couldn't help but feel sad for a while. But at the same time, I had discovered the reason why the chrysanthemums were dying. It was because the side of the house was very damp. The sun was blocked by the tall buildings of the neighbors, and there was only a little light at noon, but it only lasted for a few tens of minutes. I couldn't help but sigh for the fate of the chrysanthemums, but I also understood that "chrysanthemums will not bloom in a home without sunshine."

Regarding this, my wife seemed to have found the basis for her philosophy, saying, "The flowers you plant are not thriving, they will wither even if they bloom, what is the point? Only the paper flowers I make are the ones that will never wither."

But at that time, the sadness in my heart was not about whether the flowers would wither or not.

Yarn and Cotton

Record of November Yarn and Cotton Deliveries

10,750 bales of yarn at a price of 181 yuan

9,400 dan of cotton delivered at a price of 36 yuan

The Jinji brand yarn for the November period was listed for trading on June 1st of this year. The first round price was 182.7 yuan. At this time, because North China was actively purchasing coarse yarn, the market gradually showed signs of life. Moreover, the inventory of cotton during the old cotton season was gradually thinning, and prices were rising. The factory felt it was difficult, so they had to take the method of reducing labor to compensate. Therefore, the number of people reducing or stopping work increased daily, the production quantity decreased greatly, and the market gradually stabilized. Later, in mid-July and August, the United States implemented the "Peng Hai An" policy, the cotton fields were reduced, and the price of US cotton rose. At the same time, the financial sector made large profits on wheat and flour, and turned to the yarn and cotton market, buying in large quantities. People's hearts were agitated, and the highest price of standard yarn was seen to be over 189 yuan. Before long, a large amount of silver flowed out, the price of gold fell, and the eastern exchange rate rose sharply. The national currency price of three-grade yarn was only 262.3 yuan. Japanese merchants dumped large quantities on our country's market, and the market price suffered great pressure, and the situation gradually became panicked. In addition, the exchange had thousands of bales of old goods due to expire in recent months. No one welcomed these goods, so the lowest price was seen at 170 yuan. In mid-October, in order to prevent the outflow of silver, the National Government increased the export tax on silver and added a equalization tax. The gold market soared, and prices soared all at once. The banking industry first speculated and bought in large quantities. The market price rose sharply from 170 yuan to 187 yuan. Later, those who made profits settled, and suddenly fell to 178 yuan. Extending to the recent period, due to the purchase by Tongcheng Company, preparing to receive goods, it rose again to 182.9 yuan. As a result, the remaining 10,750 bales were delivered at a price of 181 yuan. It is said that Tongcheng Company alone received 8,800 bales. The goods inspected included 2,000 bales of new goods, 1,300 bales of 20-count Fugui, 100 bales of Hongren, 200 bales of Ren, 250 bales of Baoyi, 200 bales of Shepherd, and the rest were expired goods. [N]orthern and Southern Goods

Raw Peanuts Telegram Indicates Price Drop

Qingdao Telegram Indicates Further Slight Decrease of 12 Jiao

According to the initial telegram from Xuzhou, raw peanuts had risen to 6 yuan, while the declared price in Shanghai was 6.7 yuan, which was excessively different from the Shanghai market. Therefore, the merchants had no suitable place for their goods and remained cautiously on the sidelines. However, Guangdong merchants also kept their hands off due to the dull market in Qingdao. Both sides were gradually engaged in a standoff. Only Shandong peanuts were offered at 6 yuan, and Kaifeng peanuts at 6.1 yuan, a decrease of 2-3 jiao from the previous prices. By the evening telegram, the ground price in Qingdao had fallen by another 1-2 jiao, and the market price in the Xuzhou telegram also showed signs of wavering. The market in the future could be expected to decline. In addition, news was heard from customs that the additional tax on raw peanuts might be avoided, but no official document had been received, so it was not confirmed. This is also noted to observe its subsequent development. However, based on the ground price, the market in the future might continue to fall.

Sugar Market 186

No. 3 Fine White Sugar Opens at 17 Yuan

Yesterday, the sugar market's trend turned firm due to a slight rise in customs duties. The Public Association set the price of No. 24 raw brown sugar and white sugar at 18.95 jiao for ordinary spot goods, and 5.2 yuan for imported goods, with transactions occurring. No. 8 and 9 Dutch red sugar was priced at 14 yuan, an increase of 5 fen from the previous day, and re-exported goods were quoted at 4.9 jiao. White No. 4 continued to sell 2-300 bags, with No. 3 at 17 yuan, No. 4 at 16.4 jiao, and No. 1 not being offered. Based on No. 3, 17.4 jiao, before and after need to raise 89 jiao, other by reason, still cautious do not out. The New Tide Qing steamship arrived yesterday, with only 1011 bags, a severe shortage, therefore extremely, as soon as open. Mentioned Qing, as thirteen yuan, yellow twelve yuan eight jiao, ten yuan six jiao.

Silk and Tea 187

Silk Business Has Been Quite Active Lately

Since the British government reduced import duties on Chinese and French raw silk, silk shipments to England have gradually become smoother. The other day, the Great Britain steamer shipped 415 bales of yellow and white raw silk and 170 bales of waste silk (i.e., silk waste) to London, including 195 bales of coarse silk for transshipment to Mumbai. The Wuxi factory's raw silk, 131 bales with Double Deer and Malu patterns etc., were loaded onto the docks yesterday and the day before, waiting to be transported to foreign trading houses. Trading houses only, white filature warp from entered Shanghai sixty packages.

Metals 188

Sales of Black Iron Sheets in the North Are Gradually Decreasing

The black iron sheet business in the north has been decreasing lately, so there are fewer price negotiations and transactions in the market than before. This is because the weather in the north is already very cold, and they have already prepared for winter sales products, so there is not much purchasing. Transactions in the south are also very meager. Enamelware factories and thermos factories are also making few additions, so the market situation seems to be passing its peak season, and sales are declining. The market price of 18-sheet cargo measuring three feet by six feet is 9.89 jiao per dan, while colored sheets measuring three feet by six feet with 3 to 13 sheets are estimated at varying prices from 9.23 jiao to 10.045 jiao. It is said that only 50-60 dan were offered in the market yesterday. The inventory is quite large, so there is little hope for a turnaround in the market situation this year.
