Free Talk

Literary Sentiment 189

— Xia Shi

What is literary sentiment? This question, after we unanimously acknowledge that sentiment is a characteristic of literature, seems to require renewed discussion.

Sentiment is just an empty noun. It itself has no specific content; its content is entirely determined by how each individual perceives their own life. For example, a blank sheet of paper, dyed red, becomes red paper, dyed black, becomes black paper. Although red paper and black paper are both paper, their different hues affect people's vision, and thus appear distinctly different. Sentiment is the same; crying is a sentiment, and laughing is also a sentiment, yet everyone knows there's a huge difference between crying and laughing. Moreover, even if it's the same crying or the same laughing, it cannot be assumed that the sentiment expressed is the same. What some people laugh at, others often cry at. Therefore, if we simply say that sentiment is an element of literature in a general way, it is far from sufficient. We should further ask: What kind of sentiment is literary sentiment? What kind of sentiment can evoke empathy in readers?

Some people think that literary sentiment is beautiful and surreal. Reality is only cruel and ugly. Only an idealized world can be considered beautiful, and literature should lead people to revel in a non-realistic, ideal life.

Such a view is naturally incorrect, because they fundamentally see literature as the exclusive property of a few, separating sentiment from real life.

Since literature is intellectual sustenance for many people, the sentiment in literature must necessarily be the sentiment of ordinary people, and only this sentiment can evoke empathy.

The so-called sentiment of ordinary people is not some abstract thing, but arises from their actual lives. Sentiment that is divorced from real life is merely false sentiment. An author, if he wants his works to have rich sentiment and deeply move readers, must experience life extensively; he cannot obtain the means solely from books. Someone who has never been hungry will never understand the pain of hunger, and even if they use some scientific knowledge to express it in writing, it would be no different from ladies seeing beggars on the street, just shaking their heads and sighing, without touching their suffering at all. Compare Sinclair and Gorky. Sinclair ultimately could only be an observational socialist writer because he was not one of the common people; he was completely unfamiliar with the lives of the common people. As for Gorky, he himself was a vagrant, so naturally, the sentiment he expressed in literature became genuine sentiment, which would move readers all over the world.

Of course, the sentiment of ordinary people is not a simple thing, nor is it a monolithic thing. Their lives are complex, and the sentiment arising from life is necessarily complex. It is here that sentiment can be simply divided into two aspects: negative sentiment and positive sentiment. Faced with a drought, some people will commit suicide, while others will become enraged and think of other ways to survive. The former is the sentiment passed down to readers from the chivalric novels left over from the old society. This kind of sentiment is poisonous. If the sentiment of literature is to nourish the upward will of ordinary people, then it is necessary to eliminate those negative and poisonous sentiments from the works.

New Guest House on the Shores of Saigon (Part 2) 190

— Xin Er

Finally, we entered a desolate empty courtyard, with a patio paved with small stones in the middle. Besides the house and us, there was nothing else. What place is this? It's the new guest house, exclusively for detaining new arrivals! Exhausted, we sat down to rest, disregarding the dirt on the ground. But we were even more overwhelmed by this desolate and miserable atmosphere. How exactly are we to be dealt with? Isn't this place like a prison? Thinking of this, thinking of my hometown, I couldn't help but feel a pang of sadness in my heart. I looked at the half-new, half-old walls and the disheveled companions, sitting there dejectedly.

Fortunately, there was a large window facing the road, with large gaps between the iron bars, allowing things to be passed in from the outside. Many Annamese women and overseas Chinese were looking in from outside, many of the latter specifically to see people coming from their homeland. Many items of food were passed through the window slits. Someone was saying:

"It's dangerous. It's so late. The foreigners don't work after hours. You'll have to spend the night in the new guest house!"

Heavens, spend the night! How? Could we really spend the night just sitting on the ground, hungry? I was constantly worried and hesitant. Gradually, the commotion subsided a bit, and everyone had no choice but to sit in silence. Those who weren't getting anything sent to them handed coins out the window to the street to buy some buns and bread to fill their stomachs. My hesitation also wavered. I bought a large piece of bread, blankly preparing for the night. There were too many people, so I was embarrassed to cry.

Finally, it quieted down, and the gray-white dusk turned into night. The foreigners were confident in letting these Chinese people spend the night here. These people also spent the night well enough, spending their first night in a foreign land. But who knows how many people were secretly shedding tears in the darkness, leaving their homes and villages, their golden dreams of a foreign land dashed.

The night wasn't too cold, but there were too many mosquitoes, and there were so many confused thoughts that no one could fall asleep. The women locked in the next room were holding their crying babies, which made us feel even worse. A cold, chilling air rose from the ground, making us shiver involuntarily. Some were even crying, some were murmuring like women, some were shouting and sighing. Thinking about the scene when the ship entered the port in the morning, we felt even more miserable.

These people endured the night peacefully, but the next day they cried out in pain:

"Heavens! Today is Sunday, and the foreigners aren't working again."

The new guest house was still desolate, and inside, these Chinese people were wriggling about. Good Chinese people, why have they suddenly become like prisoners? I was disappointed and regretted it! But fortunately, some people were gritting their teeth and enduring.

Like a large pile of worms, wriggling, they spent the second day and the second night. Most could only move their hands and feet, as if they couldn't speak. No one came to care for us. It was like being stranded in a desolate desert, or being imprisoned in a small cell, without human freedom.

Sunday passed, and on the morning of the third day, this extremely disheveled group of people was driven to a large garden nearby, which was where the officials of the new guest house worked. Men, women, and children were still mixed together. When the office started, the crowd was as crowded as if they were snatching gold. I waited patiently for a long time, but couldn't help but panic, and followed everyone to squeeze forward, and was squeezed into the middle of the crowd. However, after a long time, I still couldn't squeeze through the door of the office. I couldn't breathe and was about to suffocate, so I squeezed back out. I rested for a long time, mustered up my courage, and squeezed forward again. Three or five times, I was suffocated in the middle and retreated in disappointment. Sometimes the people squeezed to the front were beaten indiscriminately by the Annamese, and the large crowd squeezed back like a collapsing dam; but after a while, they squeezed back up again. Children were trampled and screamed for their lives.

In the end, fearing that waiting too long would cause an accident, I braved the risk and squeezed in. Fortunately, I was also squeezed into the middle and mingled in. In the large office, there were many white people and Annamese working. But I didn't know whose desk to go to first. After watching for a long time, I followed others up. The first two were Annamese, and one was taking fingerprints. When I went to the desk, I just stood there blankly, not understanding French or Annamese, and no one told me what to do. What to do? In the end, I saw people holding small coins, looking under the "identity paper" and calling out "coin, coin." I followed suit, and the Annamese paid attention to me, doing the procedures for me, the entry paper, the new paper. The entry paper cost about eleven yuan, and the "identity paper" cost more than thirty yuan. After paying the money and getting the papers, I had to go through several places to sign and take fingerprints, and coins were also needed. The white people were much more imposing than the Annamese. Their gaze was frightening, and I didn't dare to raise my head, let alone meet their eyes. Once, I couldn't figure out whose gate I had to pass, so perhaps I went to the wrong person. Not only did the white person not tell me, but with a thick foot, he kicked me to the ground. This was more difficult than ascending to heaven! There was no explanation, and it was impossible to ask, so how could I know which gate to pass first? Foreigners were really difficult to deal with. I fell to the ground, and blood was about to spurt out. Some eighteen- or nineteen-year-old youths lied, saying they were fifteen or sixteen years old, wanting to avoid paying the head tax (the head tax), but the white people always gave them a few slaps, beating them severely before letting them go, or not letting them go no matter what.

Standing in the office for more than half an hour, I became dizzy. Confused, I took the identity paper and entry paper, walked out of the office, and tears fell!

Why did I come here? I wiped away the tears, asking myself.

Leaving the new guest house on the shores of Saigon, I was numb all over, and the world before my eyes was dark. My legs were sore, my hands were weak, and I couldn't even lift my head.

Occupation and Aspiration 191

— Luo Mi

A person always goes through selection from their own depths

and tacitly agrees to do one or more things that they are willing to do. But the things a person is doing are not necessarily the things they are willing to do. If we call the things a person is doing an occupation, and the things a person is willing to do an aspiration, then we can say that probably most people are living a life where occupation and aspiration are separated!

This is a common fact that we see: some can only do a little of what they are willing to do in their spare time from their occupation; some have not done what they are willing to do at all and have spent their entire lives; this is truly a great tragedy for modern people! As for the happy ones who live a life where aspiration and occupation coincide, they are probably rare, right?

Originally, doing a kind of work is a manifestation of the vitality of seeking a living. When vitality is expressed in the work that one is willing to do, one feels joy; when vitality is expressed in the work that one is not willing to do, one feels pain. Thus, modern people who are tightly bound to an occupation that is far removed from what they are willing to do are universally shouting out the bitterness felt from deeply tasting the taste of occupation!

Since living a life where occupation and aspiration are separated is painful, then why do most people feel this way and still live like that? Since occupation is not their aspiration, why not abandon their occupation? This can probably be divided into two situations: first, a small number of people cannot get the things they are willing to do, so they have no choice but to settle for second best. Like many ancient people who were not recognized by those in power, they retreated and wrote books or lived in seclusion in the mountains. Second, most people have to take up occupations that are separated from their aspirations for the sake of survival, or they temporarily take advantage of such opportunities, or they want to seek a guarantee of survival in their occupations and then do their aspirations, or they do what they are willing to do in their spare time from their occupations. There are countless people like this. And the reason is that the environment makes people willing to do certain work, but does not give people the environment to do certain work!

The occupations that everyone takes up are exactly the aspirations that everyone is willing to do. In other words, everyone is doing the work they are willing to do. Such a society will eventually come, right? As for mankind, they are always working towards this direction, I think.

At that time, a person will no longer feel bitter because of the separation of occupation and aspiration. At that time, work will not be for the sake of life, but for the service of human society!

Under that kind of life, people will become even greater!

Memories of Life in a Small Inn 192

— Wei Zhongtian

I remember very clearly that it was last year, during the season when osmanthus flowers were in full bloom, that I had a period of drifting in a place full of troops. I lived in a small inn waiting for a "job," and the days were so long and so dull. Originally, I was unfamiliar with the place, and I was also poor. When people are poor, they naturally have fewer friends, so I always dragged my long legs alone on the cold streets, on the small hills, and in the fields, pacing and daydreaming. It was autumn, the sky was so high and so blue, sometimes a flock of birds would fly across the sky, purple wildflowers bloomed by the stream, and the gentle autumn breeze would brush my face, making a lonely traveler sometimes feel a slight joy!

Living in a small inn for more than a month has given me a lot of memories to this day. At that time, the days were really hard to get through. I was poor, so what could I do to pass those days? So, the seeds of melancholy occupied my heart more and more each day. My heart seemed to be frying in a pan of oil all day long. The days passed by, but the "job" became more and more vague. My father wrote to me asking how my job situation was, and I endured the pain and wrote a moving letter to deceive my father, saying that I would have a job soon. Only I understood the hidden pain at that time. One day, I fell ill. You can imagine, a person who is poor, adrift, and sick will really suffer to death if he is weak. Fortunately, I was a traveler who was accustomed to hardship, and the illness was not very serious. A week passed, and I recovered my original health!

I remember one late night when I was sick, the small inn was as dead and silent as an ancient temple. A dim oil lamp, the size of a bean, accompanied me. I thought of everything in my childhood, I thought of the traces of struggle in recent years, and even more, I thought of the vague future. I was sad, and I shed a burst of lonely tears. Crying is a shameful act, I know. However, I finally couldn't help but shed them, those sour tears, those lonely tears…

Those who have not experienced life in a small inn do not know how much meaning it contains. I used to be in jail, and I think that being in a small inn is just like being in jail, both are the best places to experience life. To this day, I can't forget the rich knowledge that this place gave me.

In the small inn, when it is quiet, it is like an ancient temple in the deep mountains, but when it is lively, there are also those frustrated drifters singing wildly after getting drunk. On the grayish-colored walls are full of popular poems, some complaining about heaven, some complaining about the world, some complaining about fate, some are negative, decadent, romantic… I once copied all these poems into a diary, but later, during an incident, I lost it in a memorable place. Now, almost a year has passed, and I am still so regretful!

Living in a small inn for more than a month was like living for more than a year. The days were really so dull that it was a bit hard to believe. I waited for the arrival of the "job" with an anxious heart, but the "job" finally sank into the sea like a stone and there was no news of it at all. A friend wrote to me saying: "In this society, if you can't flatter and you can't lick, you still have to train your belly that is not used to being hungry!"

So, I finally left that small inn one morning with an even more bewildered heart. The emotions at this time can be described as very miserable.

Tomorrow (4) 193

— (Written by Joseph Conrad) Translated by Wu Xiangyu

Captain Hagberd had been a coasting sailor all his life. He was one of several sons of a bankrupt farmer, and he went to sea. He had become a master mariner before long, and all his sea life had been spent along the coast. Perhaps it had been an arduous life at first; he had never liked it; he preferred the land with its innumerable houses, and the peace of life lived near a fireside. Many sailors had reason to hate the sea life, but his hatred was purely sentimental—as if his preference for a settled existence had been inherited through generations.

"Many people don't know what they are making of their children when they send them to sea," he would explain to Bessie. "It's just making prisoners of them at once." He did not believe you ever got used to it. The older you grew the more you hated it. What was it? For the best part of your life never to set foot in your own house? You went away right into it without knowing what might have happened. Some people may think that he hated long voyages; but the longest voyage he had ever made would have been one of a fortnight, and during most of that time he had been at anchor dodging foul weather. Directly his wife came into a house and some money to live on (from a single uncle who had saved a bit in the coal trade), he gave up the command of the collier "East Coast" as though it had been a galley slavery. Even after all these years he could count on the fingers of both hands all the days he had been out of sight of the British coast. He had never known what it was to be out in the deep ocean. "I have never been further than eighty fathom off the land," was his boast.

Bessie Carvil had heard all this many times in the front of their cottage, where dwarf yellow trees grew. In the summer afternoons she often carried a chair out on the grass and sat down with her sewing. Captain Hagberd, dressed in canvas clothing, leaned on a shovel. Every day he dug in his small square of earth in front of him. He turned it over and over every year, but he did not "mean to" plant anything "at present."

"I shall never plant anything till our Harry comes home to-morrow," he always said to Bessie Carvil more explicitly. She had heard that formula of hope so often that it awakened in her a vague pity for that infatuated old man.

Special Supplement of Shen Bao, Local News

Idle Chat

Tempering of Leisurely Nature 194

— Chen Liang

It seems that friends who usually love activities have not been coming in and out of my house for two months now. Have they abandoned me, or have I developed a dislike for them? I have never thought about this in detail myself. In the past, I was a person who liked excitement, even when I was sleeping, I would have the noisy, strange four-tube radio on. Sometimes, I was disliked by my family and they would secretly turn it off. The sudden silence would be like pouring a bucket of cold water, shocking my soul, which had just rested, back from a cold dream. Loneliness and I were as incompatible as ice and charcoal. Naturally, I could not live in a lonely realm. However, now, I have endured two months of lonely life, which is truly an abnormal state of affairs.

The result of two months of abnormal behavior is that the radio has been abandoned under the low iron bed, the clock that announces the time has been removed, children have been forbidden from entering my room, and I have cultivated a leisurely temperament in loneliness. Although speaking is people's freedom, even if I encounter loud voices, I want to cover my ears. "Isn't it? It's neither a speech on a competitive election platform, nor the market where hands clap in the exchange, so this kind of howling that cuts through the sky is not needed!" I am secretly cursing in my heart. Many letters and invitations have been put in the wire basket. When I want to reply, my mind vaguely aches: "These are all superfluous things, hypocritically writing some perfunctory admiration and greetings on a blank piece of paper. I don't have any achievements myself, yet I am hypocritically receiving some empty compliments from others. Isn't that simply a reverse insult! Using money or gifts to exchange for a meal and saying some cliché and conventional words that I don't want to say, is that considered socializing?" I deeply hate these superfluous things.

Therefore, I spend my days hiding at home. I bought a small bronze incense burner, lit high-quality benzoin, and the gray, elegant smoky scent wafts through the silent atmosphere. The positions of the hardcover books and untrimmed books in the bookcase have been occupied by thread-bound books with azure and brown covers, with their simple colors and silent postures. The gilded flower frame of the human figure painting on the plank wall has been replaced by Yuan Kewen's regular script and Wu Changshuo's flower and bird paintings. There is often a can of light-flavored Fattal, a pot of clear pre-rain tea, and a small collection of essays on the low table near the sofa. What an exquisite and non-ostentatious arrangement for the desk! Here, you can't smell the foul smell of fame and fortune. However, there is no coffee pot, pipe, violin, and sheet music here. So, my friends have not been coming in and out of my house for two months now.

However, I do not hate solitude and loneliness, I do not admit that I am a decadent and declining youth, and I am not imitating any lofty and unconventional formula for life. I just think that this is a kind of tempering of leisurely nature. "People cannot live without reality, just as fish cannot live without flowing water. Fish love clear water and hate turbid water, so why can't people live in a leisurely environment for a while?" I often meditate in the blue-gray smoke circles of Fattal. "The turbid currents of the world are full of hypocrisy, deception, all kinds of different masks, lust for sex and fame, and infectious germs of the century. If you can't overcome them, then escape. This is exactly my time to temper myself." In this way, I have alienated friends who love activities.

Random Chats on Hairdressing 195

— Qunying

I am most reluctant to get my hair cut, but Shanghai's barbers are most adept at flattering their customers. For a "task" that could be completed in half an hour, they would meticulously trim and cut here and there as if it were a serious matter, treating your head like a work of art to be fondled and admired, often extending the process to over an hour, which is quite common. However, conversely, there are naturally some customers who enjoy practicing the art of meditation, and even at the highest price, they find it very satisfying. Forgive my impertinent remark, but our female compatriots are the representatives of this group of customers, and they can even have a lifelong record of waking up the earliest, all because of hairdressing. Recently, electric perms have become popular, and it is said that they take two or three hours or more. If you close your eyes and imagine having your hair suspended by threads and then electrified, isn't that just suffering alive?

However, on a holiday, if you have no friends to confide in and don't want to go to the cinema, the best way to pass the time is to go to the barber shop.

The moment you push open the glass door, you are greeted so warmly by the shop owner, and this kind of attentive service is hard to find in any other transaction. After you sit down on the soft barber chair, the young apprentice twists a hot towel and offers you a cup of tea, leaving you with a lingering feeling of being overwhelmed with favor. Then it's the barber's turn to ask in a low voice, and you can naturally nod to indicate whether you want a haircut or a shave, what style you want, and so on. Then, you take a stack of newspapers offered to you and browse through them at your leisure. There, you will find valuable information that you usually don't pay attention to, and it has a different flavor than reading your favorite book.

In this way, time passes quickly. Before you know it, a work of art has already been sculpted. At this time, you feel that you want the final work to pass slowly, as the last moment is so precious! Even when you leave, you feel a little reluctant to part.

If not, if you are too lazy to be interested in anything, you can sit in the barber chair and immediately close your eyes, falling into a hazy sleep. Sometimes you are accidentally startled awake by a loud noise, or perhaps the radio in front of the door happens to play a love song, and you feel that listening with your ears alone is not enough, so you forcefully open your eyes. This state of being half-asleep is something you can't even imagine when lying on a Simmons bed.

I am most reluctant to get my hair cut, but conversely, I have not become a regular at the barber shop because I am too lazy to get my hair cut. So, I often tell the barber "haircut" after and

Page 19

it greatly surprises him that this fellow doesn't know what "shaving" is!

Are there too many people who share my sentiment? When I step into a barber shop, all the seats are often occupied by those who arrived earlier, which makes me feel slightly regretful. However, once you have entered the door, the shop owner is unwilling to let go of this customer easily. He will bend over, extend his hand, and repeatedly say "please," making you feel too embarrassed to retreat. Sometimes you even hear several similar voices saying as if enticingly, "Almost done!" But in reality, perhaps their work has just begun.

They have a long bench placed in an empty space, and many newspapers are piled up there, but you are certainly unwilling to flip through them. The hot towels and tea offered by the young apprentices also don't feel warm, but rather like a form of oppression. In this kind of situation, you must make a decisive decision, and no matter how humble the shop owner's attitude is, immediately exit the door, turn your head and leave without looking back, and go to another barber shop, where you might make a new discovery.

However, many people are unwilling to do this. They have their favorite barber shop, and even more so, their favorite barber. This, of course, has its advantages. Because I have no such experience, I will omit it.

Wind and Dust 196

— Feng

｜｜Impressions of Beiping, Part Three

Speaking of Beiping, one cannot avoid mentioning wind and dust, as if wind and dust have a great connection with Beiping. The intensity of Beiping's wind and the abundance of its dust are probably due to the region beyond the Great Wall: the area beyond the Great Wall is rich in wind and sand, and when the trees shed their leaves, the wind and sand become rampant.

Now is precisely that time again. The raging winds beyond the Great Wall are sweeping into this ancient city once more. The raging winds bring news of ice and snow, sweeping away the withered and scorched leaves, until the trees are left with only bare branches trembling in the wind. In this way, when another spring comes, the trees will turn from pale yellow to light green, and the raging winds will also become gentle.

I like to watch the wind carrying dust across the vast northern plains. I remember it was during the late autumn. When I lived in the Western Hills, I would often hear the pine branches rustling like the tide. I would often climb up the mountain, straining my eyes to look at the gray plain to the southeast. I stood shaking in the wind, as rugged and proud as the ancient pines, watching the sea of dust on the plain from the mountain peak. The scene and color were truly magnificent. In the near distance, it looked somewhat like

thousands of troops and horses battling on the battlefield. In the distance, it appeared slightly blurred, like looking at a long river from the mountains on a summer morning, with the mist, smoke, and water vapor along the river winding into a white ribbon. It was also like a hundred or eighty large carts traveling across the vast plain, with the dust stirred up by the horses' hooves and cartwheels forming a winding strip. However, this was not as magnificent as the scene in the near distance. One cloud of dust rushed at another, rushing and merging into one before rushing at another. This looked somewhat like ocean waves, but ocean waves are not as lively. I love the first cloud of dust in the thousands of clouds of dust the most. It is very brave and magnificent, moving straight ahead. From it, I think of Qu Yuan's heroic sacrifice: "Come, let me lead the way." The momentum was truly like that. At that time, I would forget myself. I was a brave general, with the sound of the pines encouraging me and layers of dust as my rearguard. What did I have to worry about in the distance? At that time, my mood was truly one of merging with the wind and dust. A person in that kind of realm cannot help but become heroic. Shelley's "Ode to the West Wind" was probably written like that, with a mood of raging wind and storm, like a primitive man facing the wrath of nature and forgetting himself. The wind and dust of the North have given me such an impression.

I think the wind and dust of the North ultimately have the flavor of the North. Zhi er! Zhi er! Like a speeding bullet whistling through the air, the doors and windows tremble accordingly, emitting a rumbling sound, the electric wires vibrate, and the cloth signs flutter. A sign is blown to the ground, and then another one is blown into the street. At this time, Beiping is enveloped in gray. The streets are desolate, and people who are not oppressed by life may be sitting around a roaring stove, listening to the sound of the wind to pass their days in the wind and dust. When you open the door, wind and sand rush at your face. When you go out, you bring back a face covered in black and a nose full of mud. In this way, wind and dust will be cursed. Curse as you may, the wind and dust will not disappear because of it. Beiping will never be separated from the wind and dust, because the area beyond the Great Wall still has plenty of wind and sand. This magnificence and boldness of the wind and sand have shaped the temperament of the northerners. The wind and dust of the North ultimately have the flavor of the North.

Mr. Chen Xiangtao's Tiger Paintings 197

Song of a Traveler 198

— Huishi

Flying with the whirlwind, flying with the whirlwind, flying with the whirlwind to drift east, west, south, and north: look! The fallen leaves are so light, like a speck of dust or two in space.

Singing, singing these poignant words, I hold a broken heart that is difficult to mend, cross the green water, glide over the green mountains, drifting from my hometown to a foreign land.

At night, the northwest wind blows harder and harder, like sharp arrows. Everything on the building is silent, as if covered with a layer of frost, gloomy and melancholic. On this winter night, oppressed by the cold wind, I support my painful shoulder, sit under the dim light, the silent building,茫茫然的, only a little tabby cat is lying on the table rubbing its face with its front paws.

This is a glimpse of my wandering years that have lasted for several years and are still not over. My heart is as depressed as the surrounding atmospheric pressure: intently meditating, there are only patches of scars from life and the endless sorrow of yearning, piercing me in waves of pain.

The thought of the past long, unsuccessful life, and the thought of the uncertain future path, are the most unbearable difficulties recently. I once had the courage to go forward even through boiling water or fire, and I once acted like a tough guy who wouldn't cry even if whipped. However, the endless devastation of fate and my own inherently weak soul have left me without even the strength to groan.

Since hiding away to this place, living among a group of completely unrelated strangers, my daily life consists only of sleeping and reading. I read when I wake up, and I sleep again when I am tired of reading. I don't know how many days have passed like this. However, there is not much sleep that allows me to sleep soundly, and there are not many books that I can read to my heart's content. In this moment of extreme helplessness, the only way to comfort myself is to try to attract the surrounding external objects to soothe my mind.

I am used to it! I have tacitly accepted everything. The dirty and narrow streets, the morning vegetable stalls, the afternoon vehicles and pedestrians, the streetlights like beans at night, darkness filling the entire universe. The mottled red wall of the Earth God Temple, with its doors closed all day long, a beggar in the corner of the narrow alley catching white lice. Everything is performed in a stereotypical way. Ah, is life also stereotypical? Responsibility, obligation, always passing in a stereotypical way.

A foreign land, life in a foreign land is like this, so boring, so tedious. As soon as I think of a foreign land, I can't help but think of my hometown. Let's go back to my hometown! But I have to ask the environment again. Environment, hometown, wandering, foreign land, constantly pressing against my mind, unable to find an answer.

It is said that humans are animals with inspiration, but I only feel coldness. Baseness, hypocrisy, boasting, flattery, the four elements of the art of life, I cannot do any of them, so the instruments of torture I have received are of course deserved. Isn't that so?

Birthday 199

— Jingjia

Little Sanzi sat alone on the threshold, quietly watching the clouds in the sky. Suddenly, a burst of firecrackers not far away startled him from his thoughts. Driven by curiosity and the desire to join in the fun, he hurried towards the place where the firecrackers were being set off. Several children, about the same age as himself, were scrambling on the ground to pick up unexploded firecrackers. He squeezed in and picked up two or three. Then he wanted to find out why they were setting off firecrackers. He opened his eyes wide and looked in from the doorway, and saw a large red sandalwood table with thick red candles burning like arms, and incense smoldering in the incense burner. There was also a table of very exquisite dishes. The table was surrounded by an embroidered gold-flower table skirt. Several people were happily talking and laughing in the room.

He still didn't understand why they were setting off firecrackers. A snotty-nosed child next to him told him that it was the little master of the house's tenth birthday, and they were worshiping the gods and ancestors. He indeed saw a little child dressed in colorful clothes running around inside, looking very happy. He knew that that was the little master, the same age as himself!

He suddenly seemed to think of something and quickly asked the child next to him, "What day is today?" The child shook his head. He asked another child, and one of them told him, "Today is October 14th."

October 14th! This couldn't help but stun Little Sanzi! He remembered that his mother used to say that October 14th was his birthday. So today was his birthday! And it was his tenth birthday! The same tenth birthday as that little master!

He lowered his head and looked at the two or three small firecrackers in his hand. He thought, "Why doesn't my family set off firecrackers for me?"

He also seemed to remember his eighth birthday. He remembered that day was very happy. His mother changed him into a set of red and green flower clothes, and also gave him five copper coins. At mealtime, she especially made him a bowl of noodles, and he seemed to remember that there were two eggs in the noodles! That day, Mom didn't tell him to go outside to rummage through the trash can, and let him play outside all day.

He also thought of his birthday last year. Last year was a little worse than the year before, because his mother was sick. And Mom said Dad's business was also lost. Although there were no noodles to eat, she still gave him three copper coins, and he didn't have to go outside to pick up scraps of cloth.

But this year! He had almost forgotten his birthday! Not only were there no noodles to eat, but no one gave him even three copper coins. Because his mother had died in March this year. Dad had also married a stepmother, who beat and scolded him almost every day, and didn't even give him enough to eat. Dad was also very different from before, always in a bad mood towards him, not as loving as he used to be. So his birthday was also forgotten by himself. If it weren't for the burst of firecrackers, he wouldn't have remembered it.

But it's better not to remember it! Remembering it... for some reason, Little Sanzi felt a tingling sensation in his nose, and his chest also felt like it was being pressed down by something, making him feel uncomfortable.

"Why is my birthday so pitiful?" he asked himself. He raised his head and looked inside the door, and he saw that little master was eating very pretty cakes, and a moment later he was eating fresh fruit. This made him feel even more sad!

He cried! Tears blurred his eyes. He raised his heavy feet and walked towards his home, wiping his eyes with his sleeve.

Suddenly, his right cheek was hit with a heavy blow, followed by an angry roar:

"Undying little ghost! What time is it? Still not going to pick up some things? Dead body!"

A broken basket and a pair of bamboo tongs were thrown in front of him. The terrifying sound had long scared his tears back. He quickly carried the basket on his back, picked up the tongs, and went out aimlessly.

When he reached the point where he could no longer see his home, tears immediately enveloped his eyes again!

Seagull 200

— Xibai

The sky is so clear and bright, revealing a pure and pristine blue. Even the wandering clouds dare not sully the pure, virgin-like sacred space. Ah, what a clear and bright sky!

The vast ocean unleashes its voice, singing the song of roaring waves, stirring up the calm water surface into hills and ridges on the sea.

The dilapidated sailboat is rowed by the despondent boatman, its oars creaking and groaning in harmony with the whistling of the northwest wind.

The free seagull flaps its wings and flies in the sky, over the vast sea, over the bow of the dilapidated sailboat, now east, now west, now south, now north. ｜｜｜

Ah, freely flying! Sometimes riding the west wind forward, sometimes turning its wings to resist the west wind and soar, rushing into the sky and then descending to the sea to kiss the high tide.

Oh, has the free tongue tasted what the high tide tastes like? Isn't it a bloody and smelly odor?

Ah, flapping its wings and crying out loudly! Why? Is it to demonstrate against the high tide, or to sing a sorrowful dirge for the dilapidated sailboat?

Ah, the free cry shatters the high tide on the sea, shatters the song of the waves, shatters the creaking of the dilapidated sailboat and the melancholy sound of the west wind!

There are countless majestic and glorious imperial gunboats patrolling there. Ah, seagull, why not flap your wings and fly there, to follow behind the gunboat as its vassal, but instead hover around this dilapidated sailboat and cry out loudly? Ah, it is really to awaken the despondent people in this dilapidated sailboat from their dim nightmares, from the dream demons clinging to the glory of the past!

The free seagull carries the song of free shouting! Oh, awaken, rise up and move forward!

The seagull flaps its wings and flies forward, crossing the dilapidated sailboat, stepping over the hill-like waves on the sea, acting as the vanguard of this dilapidated sailboat, acting as the guide for the boat, leading the boat forward. But ah, this dilapidated and dying boat cannot resist the fierceness of the west wind, and the waves on the sea are frustrated, and it finally cannot catch up with the seagull!

The seagull's wings are a little tired, but it cries out loudly again! Oh, it is as if all sounds have stopped: the waves have stopped singing, the west wind has stopped its melancholy tune, the boat has stopped its creaking lament! Ah, only, only on this sea, in the clear sky, the seagull flaps its wings with a flapping sound, and the sound of its crying awakens all the slaves who are having nightmares, breaking the沉危的, groaning of all low tones!

Story Singing 202

Yao Xiaoan's Pearl Tower

Zhongxi (1040) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening "Vocational Education"

Vocational skills are most important in life. The unemployed are truly pitiable. China has four hundred million compatriots. There are too many people and too few jobs, a boundless regret. In the past, Premier Sun Yat-sen was perceptive and advocated the Three Principles of the People. The Shanghai Chinese Vocational Education Society stands strong in society. Those without jobs first seek to have one, and those with jobs seek to serve with dedication. Truly, everyone has food to eat and clothes to wear. Benefiting the masses is beyond words. Such an organization is truly admirable. Shanghai should spread its reputation everywhere. Today, magnificent buildings are grandly opened. Remarkable achievements plant seeds of blessings. Many talented people are knowledgeable. They work together to create a peak. I hope you all work harder to cultivate talents for future generations. Talents are selected without omission. Saving the countryside relies on the talents of the masses. At that time, every household will surely recite and sing its praises.

Yu Xiaoxia and Yu Xiaoyun's Jade Dragonfly

Xinsheng (1380) 6:00 PM to 7:00 PM

Opening Chapter Wu Shi Hui "Ventilation"

Small business man, Qiao Yunge, thought that although small, it was not trivial. He made a living selling the freshest seasonal fruits on the street every day. He hadn't seen Ximen Qing for many days. Why didn't he come to buy fruit? He asked his son for guidance. He asked Granny Wu at the Purple Stone Street teahouse. It turned out that Ximen Qing was secretly having an affair with Pan, and they were lovingly together all day long. He hurriedly came to the teahouse and found Wang Po speaking unclearly. Therefore, Mother Wang was terrified. Someone shouted from several houses away. He grabbed Yunge and dragged him forward, scolding him as a bandit. Too muddleheaded. Who did you listen to that made you ramble on? Without asking the reason, she slapped him, knocking him down in front of the door, bereft of ideas. Then he scolded the old thief woman. He remembered this hatred. He would rely on his five-inch-long eloquent tongue. He will make waves out of nothing. He will kill the adulterer, the adulteress, and Wang Po.

"Man Jiang Hong" 208

After Li Taihu was awakened by a passage from Yu Shuicun, he realized that without money, there is no love to talk about. Originally, Li Taihu's pursuit of Qin Xiaoxiang completely followed Yu Shuicun. Now that he has figured it out, Li Taihu packed his luggage and took a job at the Zhonghua Photography Studio opposite the Confucius Temple. The next day, Taihu leaned against the railing alone, staring blankly at the Six Dynasties Store across the street. Among the passing singing girls, there was not a single Qin Xiaoxiang. He only saw Yu Shuicun wandering at the entrance of the Six Dynasties Residence. Li Taihu hurriedly called Shuicun to come to the Zhonghua Photography Studio. Shuicun told Taihu about his plan to return to Jinan. The two talked until dark before Shuicun parted ways to go home.

National Studies 209

Miss Bingmei's Tang Poetry

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Topic (1): Looking at Ji Gate by Zu Yong

Leaving Yantai startles the traveler's heart, the sounds of horns and drums clamor in the Han general's camp.

Ten thousand miles of cold light arise from accumulated snow, on the three borders, the dawn colors move perilous banners.

Desert beacon fires encroach on the barbarian moon, beside the sea the cloud-covered mountains embrace Ji City.

Although I was not a pen-wielding official in my youth, I still wish to ask for a long tassel to discuss merit.

Topic (2): Sending Wei Wan to the Capital by Li Qi

In the morning, a traveler sings a farewell song, last night a slight rain made for an easy river crossing.

Wild geese cannot bear to hear the sorrowful sounds, the cloud-covered mountains are even more so when passing through as a traveler.

The dawn colors of the border city urge the approach of cold, in the imperial gardens, the sound of fulling blocks is plentiful towards evening.

Is Chang'an not a place for enjoyment? It only makes the years and days easily wasted.

Topic (3): Ascending the Wangxian Terrace on the Ninth Day, Presented to Prefect Liu by Cui Shu

The Hanwen Emperor had a tall terrace, on this day, ascending to it, the dawn colors open.

The cloud mountains of the three Jin all face north, the wind and rain of the two tombs come from the east.

Who can recognize the gatekeeper of the pass? The immortal of the river has gone and will not return.

I wish to seek out the magistrate of Pengze, and get drunk together in the autumn of chrysanthemums.

Topic (4): Climbing Phoenix Terrace in Jinling by Li Bai

On the Phoenix Terrace, the phoenix roamed, the phoenix has left, the terrace is empty, and the river flows on its own.

The flowers and grass of the Wu palace are buried in secluded paths, the clothes and caps of the Jin dynasty have become ancient mounds.

Three mountains are half-fallen beyond the blue sky, two streams divide White Egret Isle.

All because floating clouds can obscure the view, one cannot see Chang'an, causing sorrow.
